Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
12 min
Preference Between Two Authenticated Sayings
Rasm al-mufti rule on preferencing authenticated sayings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi tarjeeh factors to choose between two authenticated sayings when issuing a fatwa.

Core Idea
When two sayings are authenticated, the stronger authentication term or tarjeeh factor decides the fatwa.

In Hanafi iftaa, muftis often face contradictory sayings both deemed authentic. This lesson introduces the rasm al-mufti rule for preferring one over the other, based on a hierarchy of authentication terms and additional tarjeeh factors. Mastering this hierarchy ensures that fatwas are based on the most authoritative position within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base rule
Recognize that when two sayings are both mu‘tamad (relied upon), the mufti may choose either freely unless a specific tarjeeh factor is present.
This is the default position: freedom of choice.
2
Distinguish authentication terms
Learn the hierarchy: 'be yufa' and 'alayhi al-fatwa' are strongest; then 'asah' (generally stronger than 'sahih'); then 'sahih', 'ashbah', 'azhar', 'mukhtar', 'awjah'.
There is a minor ikhtilaf on whether 'sahih' or 'asah' is stronger.
3
Apply the exception rule
If one saying has a stronger authentication term (especially 'asah' vs 'sahih', or 'be yufa'), that saying becomes preponderant and must be followed.
The exception overrides the default choice.
4
Check additional tarjeeh factors
If both sayings have equal authentication terms, look for other factors: being in matn texts, saying of Imam Abu Hanifa, from zahir al-riwaya, held by majority of jurists, based on istihsan, beneficial for awqaf, harmonious with the time, or clearer in proof.
These factors are listed in the second set of verses.
5
Make the final determination
Whichever saying has the highest ranking term or most tarjeeh factors is the mufta bihi (operative position). Document the reasoning in the fatwa.
If still equal, either may be chosen, but it is safer to follow the clearer or more beneficial.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البيتان الأولان: وَإِنْ تَجِدْ تَصْحِيْحَ قَوْلَيْنِ وَوَرَدْ فَاخْتَرْ لِمَا شِئْتَ، فَكُلُّ مُعْتَمَدْ إِلَّا إِذَا كَانَا صَحِيحاً وَأَصَحُّ أَوْ قِيلَ: ذَا يُفْتَى بِهِ فَقَدْ رَجَحْ أَوْ كَانَ فِي الْمُتُونِ أَوْ قَوْلَ الْإِمَامِ أَوْ ظَاهِرَ الْمَرْوِي أَوْ جُلَّ الْعِظَامِ
ترجمہ: اور جب آپ ایسے دو اقوال پائیں جن میں سے ایک قول کی تصحیح کی گئی ہو تو وہی قول معتمد ہوگا، ( اس کی تصحیح کی گئی ہو ) الْفَتْوَى عَلَيْهِ، الْأَشْبَهُ، الْأظْهَر، الْمُخْتَارُ ذَا، اور الأوجه جیسے الفاظ سے، یا صحیح اور اصح کے الفاظ سے اور اصح کا لفظ صحیح سے زیادہ مؤکد ہے، اور ایک قول یہ ہے کہ صحیح کا لفظ اصح سے زیادہ مؤکد ہے، اسی طرح تصحیح کی گئی ہو بہ يفتى، يا عليه الفتوی سے اور یہ دونوں الفاظ سابقہ تمام الفاظ سے زیادہ قوت والے ہیں۔ اور اگر کہیں پر دو قول مسئلے میں صحیح والا جو ہو فتوی اسی دیں۔ تصحیح کے مقرر الفاظ بھی تو سن لیں اور ان کا فرق باہم اچھی طرح سے سمجھیں۔ اس قول پر ہے فتوی یہ قول حق سے اشبہ قول تو ہے اظہر مختار یہ یہ اوجہ ہے صحیح لکھیں یا یہ اصح ہے لکھیں اور ہے اصبح مؤکد یہ بھی یہیں سمجھ لیں یہ بھی کہا گیا ہے جس کو صحیح لکھیں ہے وہ اصح سے بہتر فتوی اسی پہ دیدیں۔ صحیح کے لئے ہے لکھنا علیہ فتوی (علیہ الفتوی) پہلے یہ لکھا ہو یفتی کا پھر ہو فقرہ (بہ یفتی)
البيتان الثانيان: قَالَ بِهِ، أَوْ كَانَ الإِسْتِحْسَانَا أَوْ زَادَ لِلاوقَافِ نَفْعاً بَانَا أو كانَ ذَا أَوْفَقَ لِلزَّمَانِ أوْ كانَ ذَا أَوْضَحَ فِي الْبُرْهَانِ.
ترجمہ: اور اگر آپ تصحیح پائیں دو ایسے اقوال کی جن میں سے ہر ایک قول مروی ہو تو آپ ان میں سے جس کا چاہیں انتخاب کرلیں، اس لیے کہ ان میں سے ہر ایک قول قابل اعتماد ہے، مگر جب دونوں صحیح واصبح ہوں (یعنی ایک قول میں صحیح کا لفظ ہو اور دوسرے قول میں اصح کا لفظ ہو )، یا کسی ایک کے بارے میں ) کہا گیا ہو کہ اس قول پر فتوی ہے تو یقیناً وہی قول راجح ہوگا ، یا ان میں سے ایک قول متون میں ہو، یا ان میں سے ایک قول امام اعظم کا ہو، یا ان میں سے ایک قول ظاہر الروایہ میں ہو ، یا ان میں سے ایک قول کے قائل بڑے بڑے فقہاء ہوں، یا ان میں سے ایک قول استحسان پر مبنی ہو، یا ان میں سے ایک قول اوقاف کے لیے واضح طور پر نفع بخش ہو یا ان میں سے ایک قول زمانہ سے زیادہ ہم آہنگ ہو، یا ان میں سے ایک قول دلیل میں واضح تر ہو ( تو ان تمام صورتوں میں جس قول میں مذکورہ بالا وجوہ ترجیح میں سے کوئی وجہ ترجیح مل جائے اسی قول پر فتوی دیں گے)۔ دو قول کی کہیں پر صحیح آپ دیکھیں دونوں ہی معتمد ہیں فتوی کسی یا یہ یہ دیدیں ایک تو اصح ہو اور دوسرا صحیح ہو بحث ہو چکی پھر اس کو یاد کرلو ہے یا جب کسی کے حق میں ملتی یہ بھی کہدیں ترجیح اب اسی اسی کی ہے وہ بالیقین جانیں ہ قول بھی جو ان کا مذکور متن نکلے اور ایک قول وہ جو قول امام ٹھہرے
The first two verses: And if you find two sayings that have been authenticated and reported, then choose whichever you wish, for each is reliable except when one is 'sahih' and the other 'asah', or it is said 'this is fatwa' so it has preponderance, or it is in the matn texts, or it is the saying of the Imam, or it is from the apparent (zahir) of the transmitted, or the great ones (jull al-azam) said it. He said it, or it was based on istihsan, or it adds clear benefit for the awqaf, or it is more suited for the time, or it is clearer in proof. Translation: When you find two sayings one of which has been authenticated, that saying is mu'tamad. This authentication is indicated by words such as 'al-fatwa alayhi', 'al-ashbah', 'al-adhhar', 'al-mukhtar', 'al-awjah', or from the words 'sahih' and 'asah' – and 'asah' is more emphatic than 'sahih', though some say 'sahih' is more emphatic. Similarly, authentication by 'be yufa' or 'alayhi al-fatwa' – these two expressions are stronger than all previous ones. If there are two sayings in a mas'ala, give fatwa with the one marked 'sahih'. Recognize the set terms of authentication and their differences. This saying is the one for fatwa, this saying is more like the truth, this is adhhar, this is mukhtar, this is awjah. Write 'sahih' or write 'asah', and 'asah' is more emphatic. It is also said that 'sahih' is better than 'asah' – give fatwa with it. For 'sahih' there is writing 'alayhi al-fatwa'. First write 'be yufa' then the phrase 'be yufa'. The second two verses: He said it, or it was based on istihsan, or it adds clear benefit for the awqaf, or it is more suited for the time, or it is clearer in proof. Translation: If you find two sayings both reported, you may choose whichever you wish because each is reliable, except when both are 'sahih' and 'asah' (i.e., one has 'sahih' and the other 'asah'), or it is said about one that 'fatwa is upon it' – then that one is certainly preponderant, or one of them is in the matn texts, or one is the saying of Imam Abu Hanifa, or one is from zahir al-riwaya, or one is held by great jurists, or one is based on istihsan, or one brings clear benefit for awqaf, or one is more harmonious with the time, or one is clearer in proof – in all these cases, the saying that has any of these tarjeeh factors will be given fatwa. When you see two sayings both marked 'sahih', they are both mu'tamad; give fatwa with whichever. If one is 'asah' and the other 'sahih', the discussion is done, remember it. Or if you find a tarjeeh factor in favor of one, know that one is more preponderant. The saying that appears in the matn and the saying that is the saying of the Imam.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage presents a rasm al-mufti rule for preferring between two contradictory sayings both of which have been authenticated (tasheeh). The text explains that in principle, when both sayings are mu'tamad, the mufti may choose either. However, there are exceptions and preference factors. First, the text discusses the strength of authentication terms: 'sahih' and 'asah' – 'asah' is generally more emphatic, though some reverse it. The strongest indicators are 'be yufa' and 'alayhi al-fatwa'. Second, the text lists tarjeeh factors: if the saying is in the matn texts, is the saying of Imam Abu Hanifa, from zahir al-riwaya, held by great jurists, based on istihsan, beneficial for awqaf, harmonious with the time, or clearer in dalil. If one of these applies, that saying becomes preponderant and must be given fatwa. The passage guides the mufti on how to navigate between multiple authentic positions.

Key Terms
تصحیح (tasheeh): Authentication of a legal saying by marking it with terms like 'sahih', 'asah', 'be yufa', etc.
صحیح (sahih): A term indicating a saying is authentic; its strength relative to 'asah' is debated, but it is one of the standard tasheeh terms.
اصح (asah): A term indicating a saying is more authentic or stronger than 'sahih' in the context of tasheeh.
بہ یفتی (be yufa): A phrase indicating that this is the position on which fatwa is given; considered very strong.
علیہ الفتوی (alayhi al-fatwa): Exactly synonymous with 'be yufa', indicating the relied-upon fatwa position.
استحسان (istihsan): A source of law based on juristic preference; a saying based on istihsan is preferred over one that is not.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this rasm rule, what should a mufti do when he finds two sayings both authenticated (sahih), but one is also marked 'asah'?
A) He may choose either saying freely.
B) He must follow the saying marked 'asah'.
C) He must follow the saying marked 'sahih'.
D) He must issue a joint fatwa.

Key Takeaway
The rule provides a clear hierarchy: stronger tasheeh terms and additional tarjeeh factors guide the mufti in preferencing between two authenticated sayings.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
6 min
The Ten Preference Factors for a Mufti (Rasm al-Mufti)
Fatwa hierarchy – ten tarjih factors

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to recite and apply the ten preference factors to determine the preponderant ruling when transmitted Hanafi rulings conflict.

Core Idea
Ten factors, from textual authority to temporal suitability, decide which conflicting ruling a mufti must adopt.

A mufti often encounters multiple transmitted rulings on the same issue. Which should he give fatwa on? This passage provides a clear hierarchy of ten preference factors (tarjih), derived from classical Hanafi rasm al-mufti works. Memorizing these factors is essential for reliable fatwa practice.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scenario of conflicting tasheeh
When two rulings are both transmitted and one is graded 'sahih' and the other 'asahh', the 'asahh' is automatically preponderant even before checking other factors. This is the first rule.
If one ruling is explicitly stated as the mufta bihi (the one fatwa is on), that also takes precedence.
2
Memorize the ten preference factors
List all ten factors in order: (1) the ruling is explicitly said to be the one fatwa is on; (2) it is from Imam Abu Hanifa; (3) it is in Zahir al-Riwayah; (4) it is in the matun (core texts); (5) it is followed by the majority of great jurists; (6) it is based on istihsan; (7) it brings clear benefit for endowments; (8) it is more suitable for the current time; (9) it is clearer in evidence; (10) it was stated by a reliable scholar (qāla bihī).
The Arabic couplet condenses factors 6-10; the Urdu commentary adds the first five.
3
Recognize the implicit priority among factors
Not all factors are equal. For example, if one ruling is from Imam Abu Hanifa and another is in the matun but not from him, the Imam's ruling takes precedence. Similarly, Zahir al-Riwayah rulings outweigh later nawadir.
The text says 'when both are sahih and asahh, the asahh is preponderant' – this overrides all other factors.
4
Apply the factors to a scenario
Given a concrete case with two conflicting rulings, identify which factor(s) apply to each and select the one with the strongest or most numerous factors.
If no factor applies clearly, the mufti may choose any reliable ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ بِهِ، أَوْ كَانَ الإِسْتِحْسَانَا ٦٤ أو زَادَ لِلاوقَافِ نَفْعاً بَانَا أوْ كانَ ذَا أَوْفَقَ لِلزَّمَانِ ۲۵ أوْ كانَ ذَا أَوْضَحَ فِي الْبُرْهَانِ ترجمہ: اور اگر آپ تصحیح پائیں دو ایسے اقوال کی جن میں سے ہر ایک قول مروی ہو تو آپ ان میں سے جس کا چاہیں انتخاب کرلیں ، اس لیے کہ ان میں سے ہر ایک قول قابل اعتماد ہے، مگر جب دونوں صحیح واصبح ہوں (یعنی ایک قول میں صحیح کا لفظ ہو اور دوسرے قول میں اصح کا لفظ ہو ) ، یا کسی ایک کے بارے میں ) کہا گیا ہو کہ اس قول پر فتوی ہے تو یقیناً وہی قول راجح ہوگا ، یا ان میں سے ایک قول متون میں ہو، یا ان میں سے ایک قول امام اعظم کا ہو، یا ان میں سے ایک قول ظاہر الروایہ میں ہو ، یا ان میں سے ایک قول کے قائل بڑے بڑے فقہاء ہوں، یا ان میں سے ایک قول استحسان پر مبنی ہو، یا ان میں سے ایک قول اوقاف کے لیے واضح طور پر نفع بخش ہو یا ان میں سے ایک قول زمانہ سے زیادہ ہم آہنگ ہو، یا ان میں سے ایک قول دلیل میں واضح تر ہو ( تو ان تمام صورتوں میں جس قول میں مذکورہ بالا وجوہ ترجیح میں سے کوئی وجہ ترجیح مل جائے اسی قول پر فتوی دیں گے)۔

دو قول کی کہیں پر صحیح آپ دیکھیں دونوں ہی معتمد ہیں فتوی کسی یا یہ یہ دیدیں ایک تو اصح ہو اور دوسرا صحیح ہو بحث ہو چکی پھر اس کو یاد کرلو ہے یا جب کسی کے حق میں ملتی یہ بھی کہدیں ترجیح اب اسی اسی کی ہے وہ بالیقین جانیں ہ قول بھی جو ان کا مذکور متن نکلے اور ایک قول وہ جو قول امام ٹھہرے

یا ایک قول ان میں ہو ظاہر الروایہ یا پھر بڑوں نے ہم کو وہ قول ہو بتایا شرح عقود رسم المفى ا یا قول وہ جو ٹھہرے استحسان کا نتیجہ یا وقف کے لئے ہو وہ قول فائدے کا یا قول وہ زمانہ کے حسب حال ٹھہرے یا قول وہ درایت میں سب سے بڑھ کے نکلے

هَذَا إِذَا تَعَارَضَ التَّصْحِيحُ ٢٦ أَوْ لَمْ يَكُنْ أَصْلاً بِهِ تَصْرِيحُ فَتَأْخُذُ الَّذِى لَهُ مُرَبِّحُ ٦٧ مِمَّا عَلِمْتَهُ، فَهَذَا الْأَوْضَحُ ترجمہ: یہ ترجیح والی بات اس صورت میں ہے جب کہ دو اقوال کی تصحیح میں تعارض ہو جائے یا شیح کی بالکل صراحت نہ ہو، پس اس قول پر عمل کرو جس قول میں ان مرجحات میں سے کوئی وجہ ترجیح ہو جن کو آپ جان چکے ہیں، پس یہ نہایت واضح بات ہے۔ یہ جب ہے جب تعارض تصحیح میں کہیں ہو یا جب ہے جب کہ کوئی تصریح ہی نہیں ہو اب آپ قول وہ لیں ترجیح جس کی دیکھیں کل دس وجوہ ترجیح یہ تھیں جو پڑھ چکے ہیں
He said by it, or it was istihsan, or it added clear benefit for endowments, or it was more suitable for the time, or it was clearer in proof. Translation: And if you find two such statements each transmitted, you may choose any, for each is reliable. But when both are sahih and asahh (one is sahih, the other asahh), or it is said that fatwa is on one, certainly that is preponderant. Or one is in the matun, or one is from Imam A'zam, or one is in Zahir al-Riwayah, or one is followed by great jurists, or one is based on istihsan, or one is clearly beneficial for endowments, or one is more in harmony with the times, or one is clearer in evidence – then give fatwa on the one with any of these preference factors. This is when there is conflict in tasheeh or no explicit tasreeh. So take the one that has a preponderant factor from what you have learned. This is the clearest. These ten factors are what you have read.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage is a rasm al-mufti rule: when a mufti finds two transmitted rulings that appear equally authentic, he should not randomly choose. Instead, he applies a hierarchy of ten preference factors. The text begins with the Arabic couplet enumerating factors: (1) the ruling is itself stated by a reliable scholar, (2) istihsan-based, (3) clearly beneficial for endowments, (4) more suitable for contemporary circumstances, (5) clearer in evidence. The Urdu commentary expands: the mufti may originally choose any, but when one is marked 'sahih' and the other 'asahh', the 'asahh' is preponderant. Also if it is stated that fatwa is on it, then it is certainly preponderant. The nine factors listed are: (a) it is in the matun, (b) it is from Imam Abu Hanifa, (c) it is from Zahir al-Riwayah, (d) it is followed by the great jurists, (e) it is based on istihsan, (f) it brings clear benefit for awqaf, (g) it is more in tune with the time, (h) it is clearer in evidence. The concluding couplet specifies that this selection method applies when there is a conflict in tasheeh (one said 'sahih', another 'asahh') or when there is no explicit tasreeh at all. Then the mufti looks for any of these ten factors. The number 'ten' includes the two from the first couplet. The passage is authoritative for a mufti's methodology in internal Hanafi tarjih.

Key Terms
تصحیح (tasheeh): A statement from a scholar that a particular ruling is 'sahih' (correct) within the madhhab.
ظاہر الروایہ (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani containing the authoritative transmitted rulings of the early Hanafi imams.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT one of the factors for preferring one ruling over another?
A) The ruling is from Imam Abu Hanifa
B) The ruling is based on istihsan
C) The ruling is from Imam Shafi'i
D) The ruling is clearer in evidence

Key Takeaway
A mufti must use the ten preference factors to resolve conflicting Hanafi rulings, with asahh and explicit fatwa statements as the strongest indicators.

Tarjih When Tashih is Conflicting or Absent
Rule for preferring narrations when tashih is conflicting or absent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rasm al-mufti rule that when tashih is conflicting or absent, the mufti must rely on the known murajjih (preference factors) to select the strongest narration for fatwa.

Core Idea
When correction conflicts or is absent, preference factors (murajjih) determine the mufta bihi.

This lesson presents a foundational rule from the Hanafi Rasm al-Mufti: when the later scholars have not clearly corrected one narration over another, or when there is no explicit corrected text, the mufti must use the known preference factors (murajjih) to choose the strongest opinion for fatwa. This rule ensures consistency and prevents arbitrary selection. The author refers to ten specific factors that should be learned and applied.

Guided Path
1
1. Identify the absence or conflict
First, determine whether there is a clear tashih (correction) from the later Hanafi scholars that mandates one narration. If there is conflict between two tashihs or no tashih at all, proceed to the next step.
2
2. Recall the ten murajjih
The mufti must have memorized the ten preference factors (murajjih) taught in Rasm al-Mufti. These include conformity with qiyas, prevalence of custom, ease for the people, etc.
These factors are assumed to be known from earlier lessons.
3
3. Apply each murajjih to the narrations
Weigh each narration against the ten criteria. Count how many murajjih support each narration.
4
4. Select the narration with the most murajjih
The narration that is supported by the greatest number of preference factors becomes the mufta bihi (operative ruling).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هَذَا إِذَا تَعَارَضَ التَّصْحِيحُ ٢٦ أَوْ لَمْ يَكُنْ أَصْلاً بِهِ تَصْرِيحُ فَتَأْخُذُ الَّذِى لَهُ مُرَبِّحُ ٦٧ مِمَّا عَلِمْتَهُ، فَهَذَا الْأَوْضَحُ
ترجمہ: یہ ترجیح والی بات اس صورت میں ہے جب کہ دو اقوال کی تصحیح میں تعارض ہو جائے یا شیح کی بالکل صراحت نہ ہو، پس اس قول پر عمل کرو جس قول میں ان مرجحات میں سے کوئی وجہ ترجیح ہو جن کو آپ جان چکے ہیں، پس یہ نہایت واضح بات ہے۔ یہ جب ہے جب تعارض تصحیح میں کہیں ہو یا جب ہے جب کہ کوئی تصریح ہی نہیں ہو اب آپ قول وہ لیں ترجیح جس کی دیکھیں کل دس وجوہ ترجیح یہ تھیں جو پڑھ چکے ہیں
This is when there is conflict in tashih (correction) or there is no explicit text at all, so take the one that has a murajjih (preference factor) from what you have learned, this is the clearest. Translation: This matter of preference is in the case when there is contradiction in the correction of two sayings or there is no explicit mention at all, so act upon that saying which has a cause of preference from those preference factors that you have learned. So this is very clear. This is when there is contradiction in tashih, or when there is no explicit text at all. Now take the saying that has preference. The ten causes of preference are those you have read.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage states a rasm al-mufti rule: when a mufti faces two conflicting narrations (riwayat) within the Hanafi school, and the later scholars (mutakkhirin) have not clearly corrected (tashih) one over the other, or if there is no explicit tashih, then the mufti must look for a murajjih (preference factor) from the known list. The author refers to ten such factors mentioned earlier in the text. This rule guides the mufti in selecting the stronger opinion for fatwa.

Key Terms
تصحيح (tashih): The process of correcting or authenticating one narration over another by later Hanafi scholars
مرجح (murajjih): A factor that gives preference to one opinion over another in the absence of explicit tashih

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when should a mufti apply the ten criteria of tarjih?
A) When there is a clear consensus among scholars
B) When there is a conflict in tashih or no explicit text
C) When a mufti prefers a minority opinion
D) When a qadi asks for a fatwa

Key Takeaway
When tashih is conflicting or absent, the mufta bihi is determined by applying the ten murajjih factors, not by personal preference.

Acting on Mafhum and the Authority of 'Urf
Rule for applying the implied meaning of transmitted customs as long as it does not contradict clear text

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two rasm al-mufti rules regarding acting on mafhum and the authority of 'urf, and apply them to a scenario involving customary practice.

Core Idea
A mufti may act on the understood meaning of customary reports unless a clear text contradicts; 'urf is a recognized source in the Shariah.

The mufti often encounters cases where no direct textual ruling exists. In such cases, he may rely on the mafhum (implied meaning) of transmitted practices and on established custom ('urf), provided they do not oppose a clear, proven text. These two maxims are fundamental to the Hanafi method of iftā'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first rule
Locate the phrase 'وَاعْمَلْ بِمَفْهُومٍ رِواياتٍ أتى'. This instructs the mufti to act upon the understood meaning (mafhum) of transmitted reports or customs.
Mafhum here refers to the general import, not necessarily a specific textual implication.
2
Identify the condition
The phrase 'مَالَمْ يُخالِف لِصَرِيحِ ثَبَتا' sets a condition: the mafhum must not contradict an explicit, proven text (nass qat'i).
If there is a clear text, it takes precedence; otherwise, the mafhum may be followed.
3
Identify the second rule
The phrase 'وَالْعُرْقُ فِي الشَّرْعِ لَهُ اعتبار' declares that custom ('urf) is given consideration in the Shariah.
The OCR shows 'العرق' which is likely 'العرف' (custom).
4
Understand the consequence
The phrase 'لِذا عَلَيْهِ الْحُكْمُ قَدْ يُدار' states that many rulings are made to depend on custom.
This is especially true in mu'amalat (transactions) where custom can specify general rules.
5
Apply the rules to a scenario
Given a customary practice, first check if it contradicts an explicit text. If not, the mufti may rely on the mafhum of that custom to issue a ruling.
For example, determining the market price or permissible terms in a sale.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَاعْمَلْ بِمَفْهُومٍ رِواياتٍ أتى ٦٨ مَالَمْ يُخالِف لِصَرِيحِ ثَبَتا وَالْعُرْقُ فِي الشَّرْعِ لَهُ اعتبار ۲۹ لِذا عَلَيْهِ الْحُكْمُ قَدْ يُدار
ترجمہ: اور آپ منقول شدہ رواجوں کے مفہوم پر عمل کریں جب تک کہ وہ کسی صریح ثابت شدہ قول کے خلاف نہ ہو، اور شریعت میں عرف کا اعتبار کیا گیا ہے، اسی وجہ سے بہت سارے احکام کا دارو مدار عرف پر رکھا گیا ہے۔
And act upon the understanding (mafhum) of transmitted reports (riwayat) as long as it does not contradict an explicit established text. And custom ('urf) in the Shariah has consideration, so many rulings are made to depend on it. Translation: And act upon the understood meaning of transmitted customs as long as they are not contrary to a clear established saying. And custom is given consideration in Shariah, for this reason many rulings are made to depend on custom.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage presents two rasm al-mufti rules. First, the mufti may act upon the implied meaning (mafhum) of transmitted reports or customary practices, provided that meaning does not oppose any explicit, proven textual ruling from the primary sources. Second, custom ('urf) is a recognized source in the Shariah; many rulings, especially in mu'amalat, are based on it. The Hanafi school gives heavy weight to 'urf, and later scholars often adopted the ruling that aligns with dominant custom.

Key Terms
مفهوم (mafhum): The implied or understood meaning of a text or custom, as opposed to its explicit wording
عرف ('urf): Customary practice that does not contradict Shariah, considered a subsidiary source of rulings

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the condition for acting upon the mafhum (understood meaning) of transmitted reports?
A) It must be from a sahih hadith
B) It must not contradict an explicit established text
C) It must be preferred by the majority of scholars
D) It must be based on qiyas

Key Takeaway
A mufti may rely on the mafhum of customary reports and on 'urf, provided they do not contradict an explicit, proven text.

Acting on Weak Opinions in Fatwa and Judgment
Rule restricting fatwa with weak opinions and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general rule prohibiting weak opinions in fatwa and judgment, identify the two exceptions (necessity and expertise), and distinguish the stricter prohibition for qadis.

Core Idea
Weak opinions are barred from fatwa and verdicts, except for necessity or expert muftis; qadis are absolutely bound to rajih.

This passage from the rasm al-mufti literature clarifies a critical boundary: weak (da'if) opinions within the Hanafi school are generally not actionable, whether for the mufti giving fatwa or the qadi issuing a verdict. However, the text acknowledges two narrow exceptions: a person compelled by necessity, and a mufti who has attained deep expertise (ma'rifah mashhurah). The qadi is held to a higher standard—his judgment based on a weak opinion is void. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for anyone issuing fatwas or serving as a judge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule
Read the first line: 'وَلا يَجُوزُ بِالضَّعِيْفِ الْعَمَل'. This establishes the default: acting on a weak opinion is not permissible. Both for the mufti and the questioner.
The term 'ضعيف' refers to a ruling that is weak in evidence or transmission within the madhhab.
2
Recognize the Two Exceptions
The text says 'إِلَّا لِعَامِلِ لَهُ ضَرُوْرَةً الى أو مَنْ لَهُ مَعْرِفَةٌ مَشْهُورَةً'. Identify the two exceptions: (1) a person who is compelled by necessity, and (2) a person who has well-known expertise (i.e., a highly qualified mufti).
The Arabic 'الى' appears to be a typo for 'أو' (or), so it lists two separate exceptions.
3
Distinguish the Qadi's Absolute Prohibition
The text states 'لكِنَّمَا الْقاضِي بِهِ لا يَقْضِى وَإِنْ قَضَى فَحُكْمُهُ لا يَمْضِى'. Note that the qadi is not allowed to judge by weak opinions at all, and if he does, his judgment is invalid.
This is stricter than the mufti: even necessity does not permit the qadi to use weak opinions.
4
Understand the Rationale for Qadis
The author says 'لاسِيَّما قُضاتُنا إِذْ قَيدُوا براجح الْمَذْهَبِ إِذْ قُلدُوا'. Contemporary qadis are bound by the rajih (preponderant) opinion of the madhhab because of their appointment terms.
This ensures consistency and predictability in judicial rulings.
5
Apply the Rule to a Scenario
Consider: A mufti is asked about a financial transaction. There is a weak opinion that permits it, but the rajih prohibits it. The mufti is not a high expert. Can he use the weak opinion? No, because he lacks expertise and there is no necessity. If a qadi were to use the weak opinion, his verdict would be void.
This exercise reinforces the hierarchy: mufti may only use weak opinions under strict conditions; qadi cannot use them at all.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلا يَجُوزُ بِالضَّعِيْفِ الْعَمَل ٧٠ وَلا بِهِ يُجَابُ مَنْ جاءَ يَسْأَلْ إِلَّا لِعَامِلِ لَهُ ضَرُوْرَةً الى أو مَنْ لَهُ مَعْرِفَةٌ مَشْهُورَةً لكِنَّمَا الْقاضِي بِهِ لا يَقْضِى ٧٢ وَإِنْ قَضَى فَحُكْمُهُ لا يَمْضِى لاسِيَّما قُضاتُنا إِذْ قَيدُوا ٧٣ براجح الْمَذْهَبِ إِذْ قُلدُوا
ترجمہ: اور ضعیف قول پر عمل کرنا جائز نہیں ہے اور نہ ہی ضعیف قول کے مطابق سوال کرنے والے کو جواب دیا جائے گا، مگر جس عمل کرنے والے کو مجبوری ہو یا جس مفتی کو مہارت تامہ حاصل ہو تو وہ ضعیف قول پر عمل کر سکتا ہے ( البتہ قاضی ضعیف قول کے مطابق فیصلہ نہیں کریں گے اور اگر کریں گے تو ان کا فیصلہ نافذ نہیں ہوگا، خاص طور پر ہمارے زمانے کے قاضی، اس لیے کہ انھیں مذہب کے راجح قول کے مطابق فیصلہ کرنے کا پابند بنایا گیا ہے جب انھیں قضا کا عہدہ سونپا گیا۔
And acting upon the weak (opinion) is not permissible, nor is the one who comes asking to be answered with it, except for a practitioner who has a necessity, or one who has well-known expertise. However, the qadi does not judge with it, and if he judges, his judgment does not pass—especially our judges, for they are bound by the preponderant (rajih) opinion of the madhhab, since they were appointed. Translation: And acting on a weak opinion is not permissible, nor will the questioner be answered according to a weak opinion, except for the one who is compelled (by necessity) or the mufti who has full expertise. However, the qadi will not judge according to a weak opinion, and if he does, his judgment will not be executed, especially our judges, because they are restricted to the preponderant opinion of the madhhab, as they were appointed (to follow that).
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage provides a crucial rasm al-mufti rule regarding weak (da'if) opinions within the Hanafi school. The general rule is that weak opinions are not to be acted upon nor given as fatwa. However, two exceptions exist: (1) a lay person or practitioner who is compelled by necessity (dharurah) may act on a weak opinion, and (2) a mufti who has attained full expertise (ma'rifah mashhurah) may also act on it. Importantly, a qadi is never allowed to judge by a weak opinion; if he does, his verdict is void and not enforceable. The author emphasizes that contemporary judges are bound by the rajih (preponderant) position of the madhhab as per their appointment terms. This rule preserves the consistency of judicial rulings.

Key Terms
ضعيف (da'if): A weak ruling within the madhhab that is not relied upon for fatwa or judgment except under specific conditions
معرفة مشهورة (ma'rifah mashhurah): Well-known expertise in fiqh and usul, enabling a mufti to discern when acting on a weak opinion is permissible

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, is a qadi permitted to give a verdict based on a weak opinion?
A) Yes, if the weak opinion is from a reliable source
B) No, and if he does, the verdict is not enforceable
C) Yes, if the litigants agree to it
D) No, but the verdict becomes valid if no objection is raised

Key Takeaway
Weak opinions are generally prohibited in fatwa and judgment, but a mufti may use them in cases of necessity or if he has deep expertise; a qadi is never allowed to use them.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Weak Reports in Fatwa and Qada – Conditions and Exceptions
Stating the rule on weak reports and its exceptions for mufti and qadi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which a weak report may be used in fatwa, distinguish the rules for mufti versus qadi, and apply the Hanafi hierarchy of evidence in ifta.

Core Idea
Weak reports may guide a mufti in necessity or expertise, but a qadi must adhere to the rajih.

This lesson clarifies the Hanafi ruling on using weak reports in legal practice. While the default is prohibition, the school recognizes exceptions for muftis facing necessity or possessing renowned expertise. However, qadis are strictly bound to the preferred view of the madhhab. Understanding this distinction is crucial for proper fatwa and qada.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule
Read the opening statement: 'It is not permissible to act upon a weak report, nor is one who comes asking to be answered with it.' This is the default rule for everyone.
The phrase 'weak report' refers to opinions or hadiths that are not strong enough to be the primary basis for ruling.
2
Locate the Exceptions
Find the exception clauses: 'except for a practitioner who has a necessity, or for one who has well-known expertise.' These are the two scenarios where weak reports may be used in fatwa.
The exception applies only to giving fatwa, not to judging.
3
Distinguish Mufti and Qadi
Note the separate ruling for the qadi: 'the qadi does not judge by it, and if he judges, his judgment is not enforced.' This shows a stricter binding for judges.
The qadi is appointed with the condition to follow the rajih, so he cannot deviate even if he is knowledgeable.
4
Understand the Rationale
The passage explains: 'especially our judges, since they are bound to the preferred view of the madhhab when they are appointed.' The condition of their appointment restricts their discretion.
This prevents inconsistency in judicial decisions and maintains public trust.
5
Apply to a Scenario
Consider a mufti asked about a transaction. The rajih view says it is invalid, but a weak report says it is valid. If the questioner is in need and the mufti is an expert, he may give the fatwa based on the weak report. A qadi, however, cannot judge accordingly.
This exercise solidifies the distinction.

وَلا يَجُوزُ بِالضَّعِيْفِ الْعَمَل ٧٠ وَلا بِهِ يُجَابُ مَنْ جاءَ يَسْأَلْ إِلَّا لِعَامِلِ لَهُ ضَرُوْرَةً الى أو مَنْ لَهُ مَعْرِفَةٌ مَشْهُورَةً لكِنَّمَا الْقاضِي بِهِ لا يَقْضِى ٧٢ وَإِنْ قَضَى فَحُكْمُهُ لا يَمْضِى لاسِيَّما قُضاتُنا إِذْ قَيدُوا ٧٣ براجح الْمَذْهَبِ إِذْ قُلدُوا ترجمہ: اور ضعیف قول پر عمل کرنا جائز نہیں ہے اور نہ ہی ضعیف قول کے مطابق سوال کرنے والے کو جواب دیا جائے گا، مگر جس عمل کرنے والے کو مجبوری ہو یا جس مفتی کو مہارت تامہ حاصل ہو تو وہ ضعیف قول پر عمل کر سکتا ہے ) البتہ قاضی ضعیف قول کے مطابق فیصلہ نہیں کریں گے اور اگر کریں گے تو ان کا فیصلہ نافذ نہیں ہوگا، خاص طور پر ہمارے زمانے کے قاضی، اس لیے کہ انھیں مذہب کے راجح قول کے مطابق فیصلہ کرنے کا پابند بنایا گیا ہے جب انھیں قضا کا عہدہ سونپا گیا۔ قول ضعیف جو ہو اس پر عمل نہ کیجئے جو آئے پوچھنے کو وہ بے جواب لوٹے لیکن اگر ہو کوئی مجبور بالضروره یا ایسا کوئی مفتی ہو معرفت میں شہرہ ان کو عمل ہے جائز قول ضعیف پر بھی مجبوری اور ضرورت ہوتی ہے معتبر بھی قاضی کو ناروا ہے اس پر وہ فیصلہ دے گر فیصلہ وہ کردے وہ غیر معتبر ہے اور خاص کر جو قاضی ہم عہد ہیں ہمارے جو عہد کرچکے ہیں پابند ہیں یہ اس کے
It is not permissible to act upon a weak report, nor is one who comes asking to be answered with it, except for a practitioner who has a necessity, or for one who has well-known expertise. However, the qadi does not judge by it, and if he judges, his judgment is not enforced. Especially our judges, since they are bound to the preferred view of the madhhab when they are appointed. Translation: Acting upon a weak report is not permissible, nor will the questioner be answered according to a weak report. But if the practitioner is in necessity, or if the mufti has complete expertise, then he can act upon the weak report. (However) the qadi will not give judgment according to a weak report, and if he does, his judgment will not be effective. Especially for our contemporary judges, because they are bound to judge according to the preferred view of the madhhab when they are given the office of qada. (Urdu verse): The weak report, do not act upon it; if one comes to ask, he returns unanswered. But if someone is forced by necessity, or a mufti renowned in knowledge, they are allowed to act upon a weak report when there is constraint and necessity, and it is considered valid. For the qadi, it is improper to give judgment on it; if he does judge, it is not valid. Especially our contemporary judges who have taken an oath, they are bound to it.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi usul al-ifta concerning the use of weak reports (qawl da'if) in fatwa and qada. It distinguishes between the mufti and the qadi. The general rule is that weak reports cannot be acted upon. However, there are two exceptions: (1) a person who is forced by necessity, and (2) a mufti who is renowned for his knowledge (ma'rifa mashhura) may act upon a weak report. For the qadi, the rule is stricter: he cannot base his judgment on a weak report, even if he is a scholar. If a judge does so, his judgment is not enforceable. This is particularly emphasized for contemporary judges who are bound by the conditions of their appointment to follow the preferred (rajih) view of the madhhab. The passage thus establishes the hierarchy of authority in fatwa and judiciary, ensuring that qada is based on strong evidence to maintain consistency and public trust.

Key Terms
قول ضعیف (qawl da'if): A report or opinion that is weak in evidence according to the madhhab, not reaching the level of the preferred (rajih) view.
مفتی (mufti): Here, a jurist who gives fatwas; the passage distinguishes between ordinary muftis and those with renowned expertise.
قاضی (qadi): Judge who is bound by the conditions of his appointment to follow the preferred view of the madhhab.

D) The judgment is referred to a higher court

Key Takeaway
Weak reports may be used in fatwa only under necessity or by a mufti with renowned expertise, but qadis are strictly bound to the rajih of the madhhab.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
Acting upon Weak Opinions: Fatwa vs. Qada
Concluding rule from Nazm al-Mufti on weak opinions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the permissibility of using weak opinions (qawl da'if) in fatwa under necessity and the absolute prohibition of using them in qada, and apply this rasm al-mufti rule.

Core Idea
A weak opinion may guide a fatwa in necessity, but never a qadi's verdict.

This lesson unpacks a crucial rasm al-mufti principle from Nazm al-Mufti: when can a mufti rely on a weak opinion? The poem draws a sharp line between fatwa and qada—a distinction every mufti must internalize. The passage concludes the work, emphasizing that while necessity allows the mufti flexibility, a qadi must adhere to stronger evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two legal actors
The poem mentions two roles: the mufti (who issues fatwas) and the qadi (who gives verdicts). Note how the rule differs for each.
2
Condition for the mufti
For the mufti, acting upon a weak opinion is jā'iz (permissible) only when there is majbūrī (necessity) or zarūrat (need).
Necessity here implies lack of a strong opinion or extreme hardship.
3
Absolute prohibition for the qadi
The poem states it is nārawā (not permissible) for a qadi to base a verdict on a weak opinion. If he does, the verdict is ghayr mu'tabar (invalid).
The qadi's standard is higher; his ruling must be based on strong, reliable evidence.
4
Consequence of violation
If a qadi issues a verdict using a weak opinion, the verdict is invalid, meaning it has no legal effect.
This underscores the binding nature of qada and its stricter evidentiary requirements.
5
Reflect on the wisdom
Consider why the rule is stricter for qada: qadi's rulings are binding and affect rights, while fatwas are non-binding guidance. Thus, fatwa can accommodate flexibility, but qada requires certainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ان کو عمل ہے جائز قول ضعیف پر بھی
مجبوری اور ضرورت ہوتی ہے معتبر بھی
قاضی کو ناروا ہے اس پر وہ فیصلہ دے
گر فیصلہ وہ کردے وہ غیر معتبر ہے
اور خاص کر جو قاضی ہم عہد ہیں ہمارے
جو عہد کرچکے ہیں پابند ہیں یہ اس کے
وَتَمَّ مَا نَظَمُتُهُ فِي سِلْبِ ۷۴ وَالْحَمْدُ للهِ خِتَامُ مِسْكِ
ترجمہ: اور پورے ہوئے وہ مضامین جو میں نے لڑی میں پر دیا تھا اور تمام تعریفیں اللہ ہی کے لئے ہیں ( یہ منظومہ ) مشک کی مہر ہے۔
موتی پروچکا میں جو کچھ بھی تھے پرونے اے رب ہے شکر تیرا توفیق دی جو تو نے
رومی نے نظم مفتی بارہ دنوں میں
سمى قیمتی ہے اور کہنے والا مفتی ہر بات
خدا زباں سے رومی ادا ہو کیسے کہدو زباں خامہ عجز و قصور لکھدے
It is permissible to act upon a weak opinion; in necessity and need it is considered authoritative. It is not permissible for a qadi to give a verdict based on it; if he does so, it is invalid. And especially our contemporary judges, they are bound by their oath. And completed what I composed in s? 74, and all praise is for Allah, its seal is musk. Translation: The compositions I threaded in the string are completed, and all praise is for Allah, this poem is sealed with musk. I strung whatever pearls I had, O Lord, thanks for Your guidance. Rumi composed Nazm al-Mufti in twelve days. The poem is valuable, and the speaker, the mufti, every word, how can Rumi express it? The pen of the tongue writes weakness and shortcomings.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage concludes the poetic work Nazm al-Mufti. It first states a rasm rule: acting upon a weak (da'if) opinion is permissible (ja'iz) when there is necessity (majburi) or need (zarurat). However, such opinions are not authoritative for a qadi; a qadi cannot base a verdict on a weak opinion, and if he does, the verdict is invalid (ghayr mu'tabar). This distinction highlights the difference between fatwa (which may consider weak opinions under necessity) and qada (which requires stronger evidence). The poem then thanks Allah and mentions the completion of the composition in 74 lines (?) and that it was composed by Rumi in twelve days. The final lines express gratitude and acknowledge human limitation. This summary encapsulates a key rasm al-mufti principle: the permissibility of using weak opinions in fatwa only under duress, while maintaining the integrity of judicial decisions.

Key Terms
قول ضعیف (qawl da'if): A weak opinion, i.e., a legal opinion that is not from the strongest transmitted reports or is outweighed by stronger evidence.
مجبوری (majburi): Necessity or compulsion, a condition that allows recourse to weaker opinions.
نظم مفتی (Nazm al-Mufti): The title of the poetic work composed by Rumi on the rules of issuing fatwa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A weak opinion may guide a fatwa under necessity but never a qadi's verdict.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
6 min
First Principle: Fatwa Must Be Based on the Rajih Opinion
Establishing the foundational rule that the mufti must follow the preponderant (rajih) opinion in his madhhab.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that a Hanafi mufti must base his fatwa on the rajih (preponderant) opinion and identify the exceptional cases where a marjuh (weak) opinion may be used.

Core Idea
Fatwa must follow the rajih opinion; acting on a marjuh opinion is following desire and is haram by consensus.

This lesson introduces the foundational principle of Hanafi fatwa: the mufti must adhere to the preponderant opinion (rajih) within the madhhab. The passage, drawn from 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti and its commentary by Ibn 'Abidin, establishes this as a matter of consensus (ijma') and warns against the dangers of following weak opinions. We will unpack the definitions, examine the supporting evidence from leading scholars, and understand the rare exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The mufti must give fatwa on the rajih opinion; acting upon a marjuh opinion is not permitted under normal circumstances. This is the first principle of rasm al-mufti.
2
Define key terms: rajih, marjuh, ashab al-tarjih
Rajih is the preponderant opinion; marjuh is the outweighed one. Ashab al-tarjih are the scholars who determine which opinion is rajih. Understand these classifications to apply the principle correctly.
3
Examine the proof: consensus (ijma')
Ibn 'Abidin and earlier scholars like Ibn al-Salah and al-Baji transmit ijma' on the obligation to follow the rajih. This is reinforced by statements from al-Qarafi, Qasim ibn Qutlughba, and Ibn Farhun.
4
Recognize the exceptions and limitations
The passage mentions that in a few specific places, acting upon a weak opinion is allowed. These exceptions are to be learned later, but the general rule remains strict.

پہلا اصول
مفتی کا راجح قول پر فتوی دینا
شیخ عقود رسم المفتى
فقہ حنفی کے بے شمار مسائل ایسے ہیں جن کی بابت فقہاء احناف سے مختلف اور متعارض اقوال مروی ہیں، جن میں سے بعض کو اصحاب الترجیح نے راجح اور مفتی بہ جبکہ بعض کو مرجوح اور ضعیف قرار دیا ہے، ان مسائل کی بابت فتوی دینے کے سلسلے میں بنیادی اصول یہ ہے کہ فتوی ہمیشہ اس قول پر دیں گے جس کو اصحاب الترجیح نے راجح قرار دیا ہو، مرجوح اور ضعیف قول پر عمل کرنا یا فتوی دینا اجماع کے خلاف ہے، علامہ ابن عابدین شامی فرماتے ہیں: اس شخص پر جو خود عمل کرنا چاہتا ہو یا دوسروں کو فتوی دینا چاہتا ہو لازم ہے کہ وہ اس قول کی پیروی کرے جس کو اس کے مذہب کے علماء نے راجح قرار دیا ہے، پس اس کے لیے (عام حالات میں) مرجوح قول پر عمل کرنا یا فتوی دینا جائز نہیں ہے، سوائے چند مقامات کے کہ ان میں ضعیف قول پر عمل کرنے اور فتوی دینے کی گنجائش ہے) جیسا کہ نظم میں (ان مقامات کا تذکرہ) آئے گا۔ (شرح عقود رسم المفتی: ٤٣)
علامہ ابن عابدین شامی نے اس اصول کی تائید میں چھ فقہاء کرام کے اقوال نقل کئے ہیں جو بالترتیب درج ذیل ہیں:
۱۔ محقق ابن حجر مکی کی "الفتاوی الکبری" میں ہے: امام نووی نے زوائد الروضہ میں لکھا ہے کہ مفتی اور عمل کرنے والے کے لیے جائز نہیں ہے کہ وہ بغیر غور وفکر کئے ہوئے دو قولوں یا دو وجہوں میں سے جس پر چاہے فتوی دے یا عمل کرے اور اس سلسلہ میں کسی کا اختلاف نہیں ہے، اور زوائد الروضہ کے مصنف سے پہلے علامہ ابن الصلاح نے مفتی اور عمل کرنے والے دونوں کے سلسلہ میں اور علامہ باجی مالکی نے صرف مفتی کے سلسلے میں (راجح قول پر فتوی کے واجب ہونے اور مرجوح قول پر فتوی کے عدم جواز پر) اجتماع نقل کیا ہے۔
(شرح عقود رسم المفتى: ٤٤)
۲۔ امام ابوالعباس شہاب الدین احمد بن ادریس القرافی کا کلام بھی اسی پر دلالت کرتا ہے کہ مجتہد اور مقلد دونوں کے لیے مرجوح قول پر فیصلہ کرنا اور فتوی دینا جائز نہیں ہے، اس لیے کہ یہ تو خواہش کی پیروی کرنا ہے جو بالا جماع حرام ہے، اور اس حرمت کا مصداق مجتہد فی المذہب کے بارے میں وہ صورت ہے جب کہ دلائل ان کے نزدیک متعارض نہ ہوں اور وہ ترجیح سے عاجز نہ ہوں، کیوں کہ مجتہد مقلد کے لیے اس وقت (یعنی جب دلائل میں تعارض ہو اور وہ ترجیح سے عاجز ہو) دو قولوں میں سے (کسی بھی) ایک قول پر فیصلہ کرنا بالا جماع جائز ہے۔
(شرح عقود رسم المفتى: ٤٤)
۳۔ علامہ قاسم بن قطلوبغا نے اپنی کتاب الترجیح والتصحیح للقدوری کے شروع میں کہا ہے کہ مجھے اس شخص کے بارے میں معلوم ہے جو ہمارے ائمہ کے مذہب کے سلسلے میں اپنی خواہشات پر عمل کرتا ہے حتی کہ بعض قاضیوں کی زبانی میں نے یہ بات بھی سنی ہے کہ اس میں کیا حرج ہے؟ تو میں نے کہا کہ ہاں! ضعیف قول پر فتوی دینے میں حرج ہے، اس لیے کہ نفسانی خواہش کی پیروی کرنا حرام ہے اور راجح قول کے مقابلے میں مرجوح قول معدوم کے درجہ میں ہے۔
(شرح عقود رسم المفتى: ٤٥)
۴۔ علامہ برہان الدین ابراہیم بن علی ابن فرحون یعمری کی تبصرۃ الحکام فی اصول الاقضیۃ ومناہج الاحکام میں ہے کہ جو شخص دو روایتوں یا دو اقوال میں سے مشہور قول وروایت پر مطلع نہ ہو تو اس کے لیے اپنی خواہش کی اتباع کرنا اور ترجیح میں غور و فکر کئے بغیر ان دونوں میں سے جس پر چاہے فیصلہ کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔
(شرح عقود رسم المفتى: ٤٥)
First Principle: The mufti giving fatwa based on the rajih opinion.
[Shaykh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti]
There are countless issues in Hanafi fiqh regarding which different and contradictory statements are narrated from the Hanafi jurists; among them, some have been deemed rajih (preponderant) and mufta bih (the basis for fatwa) by the scholars of tarjih, while others have been deemed marjuh (weak) and da'if (weak). The fundamental principle regarding giving fatwa on these issues is that fatwa will always be given on that opinion which the scholars of tarjih have deemed rajih. Acting upon a marjuh and weak opinion or giving fatwa based on it is contrary to ijma' (consensus). 'Allamah Ibn 'Abidin al-Shami says: It is obligatory upon the person who wants to act himself or give fatwa to others to follow the opinion which the scholars of his madhhab have deemed rajih. Thus, it is not permissible for him (under normal circumstances) to act upon or give fatwa based on the marjuh opinion, except in a few places where there is leeway to act upon and give fatwa based on the weak opinion, as will come in the poem (mention of those places). (Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 43)
'Allamah Ibn 'Abidin al-Shami has quoted the statements of six noble jurists in support of this principle, which are as follows in order:
1. In al-Fatawa al-Kubra of Muhaqqiq Ibn Hajar al-Makki: Imam al-Nawawi wrote in Zawa'id al-Rawdah that it is not permissible for the mufti and the person acting to give fatwa or act upon whichever of two statements or two aspects they wish without reflection and consideration, and there is no disagreement in this matter. Before the author of Zawa'id al-Rawdah, 'Allamah Ibn al-Salah transmitted consensus for both the mufti and the person acting, and 'Allamah al-Baji al-Maliki transmitted consensus for the mufti alone (regarding the obligation of giving fatwa on the rajih opinion and the impermissibility of giving fatwa on the marjuh opinion). (Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 44)
2. The statement of Imam Abu al-'Abbas Shihab al-Din Ahmad ibn Idris al-Qarafi also indicates that it is not permissible for both the mujtahid and the muqallid to judge and give fatwa based on the marjuh opinion, because that is following desire, which is haram by consensus. The application of this prohibition for the mujtahid fi al-madhhab is when the evidences are not contradictory in his view and he is not incapable of tarjih. Because for the mujtahid muqallid, at that time (i.e., when the evidences are contradictory and he is incapable of tarjih), it is permissible by consensus to judge based on any one of the two statements. (Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 44)
3. 'Allamah Qasim ibn Qutlubugha said at the beginning of his book al-Tarjih wa al-Tashih li al-Quduri: I know about the person who acts upon his desires regarding the madhhab of our imams, to the extent that I have heard from some judges saying, 'What harm is there in this?' So I said, 'Yes! There is harm in giving fatwa based on the weak opinion, because following one's desire is haram, and the marjuh opinion is in the rank of non-existent compared to the rajih opinion.' (Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 45)
4. In Tabsirat al-Hukkam fi Usul al-Aqdiyah wa Manahij al-Ahkam of 'Allamah Burhan al-Din Ibrahim ibn 'Ali Ibn Farhun al-Ya'mari: A person who is unaware of the well-known statement and narration among two narrations or two statements — it is not permissible for him to follow his desire and to judge based on whichever of the two he wishes without consideration and reflection in tarjih. (Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 45)
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage establishes the first principle of mufti conduct according to the Hanafi tradition: a mufti must base his fatwa on the rajih (preponderant) opinion within the madhhab, not on weak or marjuh opinions. The author, drawing from 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti and its commentary by Ibn 'Abidin, emphasizes that this is a matter of consensus (ijma'). The principle is supported by quotes from four scholars: (1) Ibn Hajar al-Makki reports from Imam Nawawi that a mufti cannot arbitrarily choose between conflicting opinions without proper tarjih; (2) Al-Qarafi states that following a marjuh opinion is tantamount to following desire, which is haram by consensus, though he notes an exception when a mujtahid cannot resolve a conflict; (3) Qasim ibn Qutlubugha equates acting on a weak opinion to non-existence; (4) Ibn Farhun forbids preference without knowledge. The passage thus lays down a strict rule: the mufti must adhere to the tarjih of his madhhab's leading scholars, with limited exceptions to be mentioned later.

Key Terms
راجح (rajih): The preponderant opinion among conflicting statements in the Hanafi madhhab, as determined by the scholars of tarjih (ashab al-tarjih). It is the basis for fatwa.
مرجوح (marjuh): The outweighed or weak opinion among conflicting statements; it is not to be acted upon or given as fatwa under normal circumstances.
اصحاب الترجیح (ashab al-tarjih): The scholars specialized in weighing and preferring one opinion over another within the Hanafi madhhab. Their determination of rajih is authoritative.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on a Hanafi mufti giving a fatwa based on a marjuh (weak) opinion under normal circumstances?
A) It is permissible (ja'iz) as long as the opinion is from a qualified Hanafi scholar.
B) It is not permissible (haram) because it is tantamount to following desires and violates consensus.
C) It is recommended (mustahabb) to choose the easier opinion for people.
D) It is only permissible if the mufti is an imam of the madhhab.

Key Takeaway
The foundation of Hanafi fatwa: always follow the rajih opinion; running after marjuh is prohibited by consensus.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
Prohibition of Fatwa on Weak Opinions
Scholarly affirmations prohibiting fatwa on weak opinions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi rule that fatwa must be based on the strong (rajih) opinion and apply the consensus (ijma) prohibition against giving fatwa on weak (marjuh) opinions.

Core Idea
Giving fatwa on a weak opinion is following desire, prohibited by consensus.

This lesson presents a series of authoritative statements from Hanafi and Maliki scholars, all affirming a fundamental rule of ifta: it is not permissible to issue a fatwa based on a weak opinion when a strong opinion is available. The underlying rationale is that doing so constitutes following one's whim, which is unanimously forbidden. Consensus (ijma) is cited as the primary proof. You will learn the rule, its evidence, its exception for cases of conflicting evidence, and the ethical obligation of a mufti to exercise tarjih (preponderance).

Guided Path
1
Identify the core rule
Read the passage and extract the central legal ruling: It is impermissible (jā'iz) for both the mujtahid and muqallid to give fatwa or judge based on a weak (marjuh) opinion.
The rule is affirmed by multiple scholars and described as a matter of consensus.
2
Understand the basis: ijma
Note that the primary evidence for the rule is consensus (ijma). The passage explicitly states that following desire is 'prohibited by consensus' and that acting on weak opinions is 'acting against consensus'.
Ijma is a primary source of Islamic law; its invocation here makes the rule binding.
3
Recognize the exception
Identify the exception mentioned by al-Qarafi: when the mujtahid within the madhhab faces conflicting evidences and is unable to perform tarjih (preponderate), it is permissible by consensus to choose either opinion.
This exception applies only when tarjih is impossible, not when the mufti simply prefers a weaker view.
4
Apply to the mufti's practice
Consider the practical implication: a mufti must investigate the well-known (mashhūr) and strong opinion in the madhhab. Giving fatwa arbitrarily on weak opinions is a violation of adab al-mufti and exposes one to sin.
Ibn al-Salah and Ibn Farhun emphasize the need for careful consideration (tarjih).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قول پر فتوی کے عدم جواز پر اجتماع نقل کیا ہے۔
(شرح عقود رسم المفتى: ٤٤)
امام ابوالعباس شہاب الدین احمد بن اور لیس القرافی کا کلام بھی اسی پر دلالت کرتا ہے کہ مجتہد اور مقلد دونوں کے لیے مرجوح قول پر فیصلہ کرنا اور فتوی دینا جائز نہیں ہے، اس لیے کہ یہ تو خواہش کی پیروی کرنا ہے جو بالا جماع حرام ہے، اور اس حرمت کا مصداق مجتہد فی المذہب کے بارے میں وہ صورت ہے جب کہ دلائل ان کے نزدیک متعارض نہ ہوں اور وہ ترجیح سے عاجز نہ ہوں، کیوں کہ مجتہد مقلد کے لیے اس وقت (یعنی جب دلائل میں تعارض ہو اور وہ ترجیح سے عاجز ہو ) دوقولوں میں سے (کسی بھی ) ایک قول پر فیصلہ کرنا بالا جماع جائز ہے۔
(شرح عقود رسم المفتى: ٤٤)
علامہ قاسم بن قطلوبغا نے اپنی کتاب الترجيح والتصحيح للقدوری کے شروع میں کہا ہے کہ مجھے اس شخص کے بارے میں معلوم ہے جو ہمارے ائمہ کے مذہب کے سلسلے میں اپنی خواہشات پر عمل کرتا ہے حتی کہ بعض قاضیوں کی زبانی میں نے یہ بات بھی سنی ہے کہ اس میں کیا حرج ہے؟ تو میں نے کہا کہ ہاں ! ضعیف قول پر فتوی دینے میں حرج ہے، اس لیے کہ نفسانی خواہش کی پیروی کرنا حرام ہے اور راجح قول کے مقابلے میں مرجوح قول معدوم کے درجہ میں ہے۔
(شرح عقود رسم المفتى : ٤٥)
علامہ برہان الدین ابراہیم بن علی ابن فرحون يعمری کی تبصرة الحكام في اصول الاقضية ومناهج الاحکام میں ہے کہ جو شخص دوروایتوں یا دو اقوال میں سے مشہور قول وروایت پر مطلع نہ ہو تو اس کے لیے اپنی خواہش کی اتباع کرنا اور ترجیح میں غور و فکر کئے بغیر ان دونوں میں سے جس پر چاہے فیصلہ کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔
(شرح عقود رسم المفتى : ٤٥)
امام ابو عمر و عثمان ابن الصلاح نے ”آداب المفتی“ میں کہا ہے: جان لو! کہ جو شخص صرف اس بات کو کافی سمجھتا ہو کہ اس کا فتوی یا اس کا عمل مسئلہ میں کسی قول یا وجہ کے موافق ہو جائے اور ترجیح میں غور و فکر کیے بغیر ان اقوال و وجوہ میں سے جس پر چاہتا ہو عمل کرتا ہو تو وہ نادان ہے اور اجماع کے خلاف عمل کرنے والا ہے۔
(شرح عقود رسم المفتى: ٤٦)
قاضی ابوالولید سلیمان بن خلف باجی مالکی نے ایک واقعہ نقل کیا ہے کہ ان کے ساتھ ایک معاملہ پیش آیا تو فقہاء نے اس سلسلے میں انھیں ایسا فتوی دیا جس میں ان کا نقصان تھا، پھر جب علامہ باجی نے ان لوگوں سے براہ راست سوال کیا تو انھوں نے کہا کہ ہمیں معلوم نھیں تھا کہ وہ آپ کا معاملہ ہے اور انھوں نے دوسری روایت پر فتوی دیا جو ان کے مقصد کے مطابق تھا، علامہ باجی فرماتے ہیں: اور اس صورت کے عدم جواز میں ان مسلمانوں کے درمیان کوئی اختلاف نہیں ہے جن کی بات اجماع کے لیے معتبر سمجھی جاتی ہے۔
(شرح عقود رسم المفتى: ٤٦)
A consensus has been transmitted on the impermissibility of giving fatwa on a weak opinion. (Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 44) The statement of Imam Abu al-Abbas Shihab al-Din Ahmad ibn [?] al-Qarafi also indicates this: that for both the mujtahid and the muqallid, it is not permissible to judge or give fatwa on a weak opinion, because that is following one's desire, which is prohibited by consensus. And the application of this prohibition to the mujtahid fi al-madhhab is in the case when the evidences are not conflicting in his view and he is not unable to perform tarjih. Because for the mujtahid muqallid, at that time (i.e., when evidences conflict and he is unable to perform tarjih), it is permissible by consensus to judge based on either of the two opinions. (Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 44) Allamah Qasim bin Qutlubugha said at the beginning of his book al-Tarjih wa al-Tasheeh lil-Quduri: I know of a person who follows his desires regarding the madhhab of our imams, to the extent that I heard from some judges saying: 'What is the harm in it?' So I said: Yes! There is harm in giving fatwa on a weak opinion, because following one's base desires is prohibited, and the weak opinion compared to the strong opinion is like non-existent. (Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 45) In Allamah Burhan al-Din Ibrahim bin Ali Ibn Farhun al-Ya'muri's Tabsirat al-Hukkam fi Usul al-Aqdiyah wa Manahij al-Ahkam: A person who is not aware of the well-known opinion or narration among two narrations or two opinions, it is not permissible for him to follow his desire and to judge based on whichever he wishes without careful consideration of tarjih. (Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 45) Imam Abu 'Umar 'Uthman Ibn al-Salah said in Adab al-Mufti: Know! Whoever considers it sufficient that his fatwa or his action coincides with any saying or aspect in a matter, and acts upon whichever of those sayings and aspects he wishes without careful consideration of tarjih, then he is ignorant and is acting against consensus. (Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 46) Qadi Abu al-Walid Sulayman bin Khalaf al-Baji al-Maliki narrated an incident: A matter came to him, and the jurists gave him a fatwa that caused him loss. Then when Allamah al-Baji asked them directly, they said: We did not know that it was your matter, and they gave a fatwa based on the other narration which suited his purpose. Allamah al-Baji says: And there is no disagreement among those Muslims whose word is considered for consensus regarding the impermissibility of this situation. (Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 46)
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of scholarly statements from various authorities, all affirming the same rule: it is not permissible to issue a fatwa based on a weak (marjuh) opinion when a strong (rajih) opinion exists. The passage begins by citing a consensus (ijma) on this point. It then quotes Imam al-Qarafi, who elaborates that both the independent jurist (mujtahid) and the follower (muqallid) are prohibited from following weak opinions because it constitutes following whim and desire, which is unanimously prohibited. However, al-Qarafi notes an exception: when a mujtahid within the madhhab faces conflicting evidences and is unable to perform tarjih, it is permissible by consensus to choose either opinion. Next, Ibn Qutlubugha emphasizes that following desires in the madhhab leads to harm, and he equates a weak opinion to non-existence when a strong opinion is available. Ibn Farhun adds that if a judge is unaware of the well-known (mashhur) narration or opinion, he must not arbitrarily follow his desire without proper investigation. Ibn al-Salah warns that anyone who acts on any opinion without tarjih is ignorant and contravenes ijma. Finally, al-Baji relates a story where jurists initially gave a weak fatwa that harmed him, but upon learning it was his case, they switched to a stronger opinion. Al-Baji states that this practice is impermissible by consensus. The overall message is that fatwa must be based on the strongest evidence within the madhhab, not on personal whims.

Key Terms
مرجوح (marjuh): The weaker opinion or position in a legal matter, which is outweighed by a stronger (rajih) opinion.
راجح (rajih): The stronger, preponderant opinion in a legal matter, which should be followed in fatwa.
فتوى (fatwa): A non-binding legal opinion issued by a mufti on a matter of Islamic law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling for a muqallid who gives a fatwa based on a weak (marjuh) opinion without performing tarjih?
A) It is permissible if the weak opinion is from the same madhhab.
B) It is permissible if the muqallid is unaware of the weak opinion's weakness.
C) It is impermissible by consensus (ijma).
D) It is permissible only if the weak opinion is more convenient for the questioner.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must base his fatwa on the strong (rajih) opinion in the madhhab; issuing fatwa on a weak opinion without necessity is an act of following desire and is prohibited by consensus.

The Obligation to Follow the Rajih Opinion
Defining the duty of the mufti to follow the preponderant opinion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule that a mufti must follow the rajih opinion and apply it to evaluate the permissibility of giving fatwa on a marjuh opinion without tarjih.

Core Idea
A mufti must only give fatwa according to the rajih; acting on any opinion without tarjih is ignorance and against ijma.

This passage from a standard Hanafi work on mufti conduct lays down a fundamental rule for the mufti: the obligation to weigh evidence and follow only the stronger opinion. It combines a direct ruling from Imam Ibn al-Salah with an illustrative incident from Qadi al-Baji, emphasizing the gravity of issuing fatwa without proper tarjih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Extract the statement from Ibn al-Salah: it is wajib (obligatory) to perform tarjih; without it, one is ignorant and acting against ijma.
2
Understand the consequence
Recognize that acting on any opinion without tarjih is impermissible by scholarly consensus.
3
Apply the lesson from the story
Note that even fuqaha can inadvertently give a marjuh fatwa, but once aware, they must correct it to the rajih.
4
Memorize the principle
Internalize that the mufti must always follow the rajih; this is a settled rule in Hanafi rasm al-mufti.

Source Text

امام ابو عمر و عثمان ابن الصلاح نے ”آداب المفتی“ میں کہا ہے: جان لو! کہ جو شخص صرف اس بات کو کافی سمجھتا ہو کہ اس کا فتوی یا اس کا عمل مسئلہ میں کسی قول یا وجہ کے موافق ہو جائے اور ترجیح میں غور و فکر کیے بغیر ان اقوال و وجوہ میں سے جس پر چاہتا ہو عمل کرتا ہو تو وہ نادان ہے اور اجماع کے خلاف عمل کرنے والا ہے۔ (شرح عقود رسم المفتى: ٤٦)
قاضی ابوالولید سلیمان بن خلف باجی مالکی نے ایک واقعہ نقل کیا ہے کہ ان کے ساتھ ایک معاملہ پیش آیا تو فقہاء نے اس سلسلے میں انھیں ایسا فتوی دیا جس میں ان کا نقصان تھا، پھر جب علامہ باجی نے ان لوگوں سے براہ راست سوال کیا تو انھوں نے کہا کہ ہمیں معلوم نہ تھا کہ وہ آپ کا معاملہ ہے اور انھوں نے دوسری روایت پر فتوی دیا جو ان کے مقصد کے مطابق تھا، علامہ باجی فرماتے ہیں: اور اس صورت کے عدم جواز میں ان مسلمانوں کے درمیان کوئی اختلاف نہیں ہے جن کی بات اجماع کے لیے معتبر سمجھی جاتی ہے۔ (شرح عقود رسم المفتى: ٤٦)
Imam Abu 'Amr 'Uthman ibn al-Salah said in 'Adab al-Mufti': Know! That the person who considers it sufficient that his fatwa or his action in a matter agrees with some statement or reasoning, and without deliberation in tarjih he acts upon whichever of those statements and reasons he wishes, then he is ignorant and is one who acts against consensus. (Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 46)
Qadi Abu al-Walid Sulayman ibn Khalaf al-Baji al-Maliki narrated an incident that a matter was presented to him, and the jurists gave him a fatwa in which there was loss for him. Then when 'Allamah al-Baji questioned those people directly, they said: We did not know that it was your matter. And they gave a fatwa based on another narration which was in accordance with his goal. 'Allamah al-Baji says: There is no disagreement among those Muslims whose statement is considered for consensus regarding the impermissibility of this situation. (Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 46)
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage establishes a fundamental rule for the mufti: it is wajib to follow only the rajih (preponderant) opinion and not to act upon any opinion without first weighing the evidence. The text quotes Imam Ibn al-Salah, who declares that doing so is ignorance and a violation of scholarly consensus (ijma). This is a stern warning against unchecked fatwa-giving. The subsequent story of Qadi al-Baji illustrates that even fuqaha may inadvertently give a marjuh (non-preponderant) fatwa when unaware of the questioner's circumstances, but once known, they must correct it to the rajih opinion. The passage concludes that there is unanimous agreement on the impermissibility of acting without tarjih. Thus, the mufti must exert effort in tarjih before issuing a fatwa.

Key Terms
رجحان/ترجیح (tarjih/rujhan): The process of weighing evidence to determine which opinion is stronger and preferable in a given matter.
راجح (rajih): The opinion that is stronger in evidence and is to be followed in fatwa or practice.
مرجوح (marjuh): The opinion that is weaker in evidence and not to be followed in fatwa or practice.
اجماع (ijma): Scholarly consensus; here specifically the consensus on the impermissibility of acting without tarjih.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It is permissible if he is a qualified mujtahid.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must only give fatwa based on the preponderant (rajih) opinion; acting on any opinion without tarjih is ignorance and a violation of consensus.

The Need to Learn Principles of Tarjih
Introducing the second principle: the necessity of knowing the rules for weighing conflicting opinions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a mufti must learn systematic principles of tarjih and identify the consequence of neglecting them.

Core Idea
A mufti cannot rely on guesswork; he must master the principles of tarjih to distinguish strong opinions from weak ones.

This passage establishes the second foundational principle of fatwa-giving: the necessity of learning the rules of tarjih. Having understood that only the rajih opinion is permissible, the mufti now needs the tools to identify which opinion is stronger. The text quotes Fatawa Khayriyya to emphasize that this is a fard duty and that giving fatwa without research is a grave sin.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the obligation
Identify from the passage that the mufti and qadi are obligated (fard) to give researched answers, not estimates.
The passage explicitly states this fard duty.
2
Identify the sources
Note the authoritative texts cited: Fatawa Khayriyya, Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti, and Kitab al-Fatawa. These contain the detailed tarjih principles.
These sources are foundational for Hanafi ifta' methodology.
3
Understand the stakes
Reflect on the warnings: following desires or inclination toward wealth is haram, and giving fatwa is a delicate matter. This underscores the gravity of the role.
The passage links neglect of tarjih to sin and calamity.
4
Appreciate the scope
Recognize that the passage sets the stage for detailed tarjih principles to follow. The mufti must study these systematically, not rely on intuition.
The text cuts off, implying elaboration in subsequent pages.

دوسرا اصول
متعارض اقوال میں ترجیح کے اصول

جب آپ یہ بات جان چکے ہیں کہ مفتی کے لئے صرف راجح قول کی پیروی کرنا واجب ہے اور مرجوح قول پر فتوی دینا اجماع کے خلاف ہے ، تو اب آپ کے لئے اُن اصول وضوابط سے واقف ہونا بھی ضروری ہے جن کی بنیاد پر متعارض اقوال میں سے ایک قول کو راج اور دوسرے قول کو مرجوح قرار دیا جاتا ہے، چنانچہ فتاوی خیریہ میں ہے کہ اس بات میں کوئی شک نہیں ہے کہ مختلف فیہ مسائل میں سے راج اور مرجوح اقوال کو پہچاننا اور قوت وضعف کے اعتبار سے ان اقوال کے درجات کو جاننا علم کے حصول میں کوشش کرنے والوں کی آخری آرزو ہوا کرتی ہے، لہذا! مفتی اور قاضی پر فرض ہے کہ وہ تحقیقی جواب دیں، اندازے سے جواب نہ دیں، حلال کو حرام کر کے یا حرام کو حلال کر کے اللہ تعالی پر افتراء سے ڈرے، اس کے لئے نفسانی خواہش کی اتباع کرنا اور اس مال کی طرف مائل ہونا حرام ہے جو بڑی آفت اور عظیم مصیبت ہے، اس لیے کہ فتوی دینا نازک کام ہے، اس سلسلہ میں ناواقف اور بد بخت لوگ ہی جسارت کرتے ہیں ۔ (شرح عقود رسم المفتی: ٥٤) علامہ شامی کی مایہ ناز کتاب شرح عقود رسم المفتی کے اکثر مضامین میں انھیں اصول وضوابط کوتحریر کیا گیا ہے جن کی بنیاد پر راج و مرجوح اقوال میں تمیز کیا جاتا ہے اور جن کی بنیاد پر مشائخ کی ترجیحات میں تطبیق دی جاتی ہے، فقیہ العصر مولانا خالد سیف اللہ رحمانی نے بھی کتاب الفتاوی کے مقدمہ میں ان اسباب کی جانب اختصار کے ساتھ اشارہ کیا ہے جن کی بنیاد پر متعارض اقوال میں سے کسی قول کو راجح قرار دیا جاتا ہے اور ترجیح میں اختلاف کی صورت میں کسی ایک فقیہ کی ترجیح پر عمل کر لیا جاتا ہے،مولانا فرماتے ہیں کہ جن مسائل میں مشائخ حنفیہ کے مابین اختلاف رائے پایا جاتا ہے ان میں ترجیح کی بنیادیں کیا ہوں گی اس
Second Principle
Principles of Tarjih among Conflicting Opinions

When you have already understood that for the mufti it is obligatory to only follow the rajih opinion and that giving a fatwa on a marjuh opinion is against consensus, then now it is also necessary for you to become acquainted with those principles and regulations on the basis of which one opinion is declared rajih and another marjuh among conflicting opinions. Accordingly, in Fatawa Khayriyya it states: There is no doubt that recognizing the rajih and marjuh opinions among disputed matters and knowing the degrees of those opinions in terms of strength and weakness is the ultimate aspiration of those striving in the acquisition of knowledge. Therefore, it is fard upon the mufti and qadi that they give researched answers, not estimated answers; they should fear fabricating against Allah by making halal haram or haram halal. For this, following one's desires and inclining towards wealth is haram, which is a great affliction and a tremendous calamity, because giving fatwa is a delicate matter; only the ignorant and unfortunate people dare in this regard. (Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 54) In the majority of the contents of 'Allamah Shami's masterpiece Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti, those principles and regulations have been written on the basis of which rajih and marjuh opinions are distinguished and on the basis of which harmony is achieved among the preferences of the mashayikh. The faqih of the era, Mawlana Khalid Saifullah al-Rahmani, has also indicated briefly in the introduction of Kitab al-Fatawa those causes on the basis of which an opinion is declared rajih among conflicting opinions and in case of disagreement in tarjih, one follows the preference of a single faqih. Mawlana says: As for the matters in which there is a difference of opinion among the Hanafi mashayikh, what will be the bases of tarjih there? This...
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage introduces the second fundamental principle in the science of ifta': the necessity of learning the rules of tarjih. Having established in the first principle that the mufti must follow only the rajih opinion, the author now argues that this can only be done by knowing the systematic principles that distinguish the stronger opinion from the weaker one. The quotation from Fatawa Khayriyya emphasizes that this knowledge is essential and that it is fard upon the mufti and qadi to give thoroughly researched answers, not guesses, and to fear Allah. The passage then directs the reader to the works of 'Allamah Shami and Mawlana Khalid Saifullah al-Rahmani for detailed principles. The text cuts off as it begins to list the actual bases of tarjih, implying that the following pages will elaborate. The lesson here is that a mufti cannot rely on intuition; he must master the scholarly criteria for weighing conflicting opinions within the Hanafi madhhab.

Key Terms
ترجیح (tarjih): The process of weighing and preferring one opinion over another based on established principles and evidence.
متعارض اقوال (muta'arid aqwal): Conflicting or contradictory opinions on a single issue within the madhhab.
فرض (fard): Obligatory; here the duty of the mufti and qadi to give researched, not estimated, answers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the duty of a mufti and qadi according to Fatawa Khayriyya as quoted in the text?
A) Give fatwa based on any available opinion.
B) Give researched answers, not estimates.
C) Follow the majority opinion.
D) Ask senior scholars before answering.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must learn and apply systematic principles of tarjih to correctly identify the stronger opinion within the Hanafi school.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
7 min
Five Bases for Tarjih Among Conflicting Rulings
Introducing five bases for tarjih in Hanafi fatwa methodology

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the five bases for tarjih among conflicting Hanafi rulings and apply them to determine the preponderant opinion.

Core Idea
Tarjih is disciplined: personality, transmission, book-type, evidence, and wording decide the stronger opinion.

This passage lays the foundation for the mufti's most critical skill: distinguishing the preponderant (rajih) from the outweighed (marjuh) opinion. The author, following Allama Shami and Maulana Khalid Saifullah Rahmani, presents five clear bases for tarjih that transform what might seem like a subjective choice into a systematic methodology. As you work through these principles, you will see how the Hanafi tradition ensures that fatwas rest on reliable foundations, not personal inclination.

Guided Path
1
Understand the necessity of tarjih
Recognize that a mufti must only issue fatwa based on the rajih opinion; acting otherwise violates consensus. This principle makes tarjih not optional but obligatory.
2
Analyze the first base: personality
Examine how the rank of the jurist (e.g., mujtahid mutlaq vs. mujtahid murajjih) affects the weight of their opinion. Higher rank generally yields a stronger opinion.
This is a matter of the authority of the scholar, not ad hominem.
3
Analyze the second base: transmission
Identify the source of transmission: Zahir al-Riwayah (from the six authoritative books) is preferred over Riwayat al-Nawadir (rare transmissions). Trace the chain back to the reliability of the narrators.
Zahir al-Riwayah has stronger chains.
4
Analyze the third base: book type
Distinguish between matn (core text) and sharh (commentary). Matn takes precedence because its authors deliberately selected reliable opinions from the madhhab, while shuruh may include weaker views.
The rule: matn over sharh.
5
Analyze the fourth and fifth bases: evidence and wording
For evidence: istihsan outweighs qiyas. For wording: explicit terms like 'asahh' indicate the author's preference and are given weight in tarjih.
These two bases rely on substantive and textual signals respectively.

Source Text
