دوسرا اصول
متعارض اقوال میں ترجیح کے اصول

جب آپ یہ بات جان چکے ہیں کہ مفتی کے لئے صرف راجح قول کی پیروی کرنا واجب ہے اور مرجوح قول پر فتوی دینا اجماع کے خلاف ہے، تو اب آپ کے لئے اُن اصول وضوابط سے واقف ہونا بھی ضروری ہے جن کی بنیاد پر متعارض اقوال میں سے ایک قول کو راجح اور دوسرے قول کو مرجوح قرار دیا جاتا ہے، چنانچہ فتاوی خیریہ میں ہے کہ اس بات میں کوئی شک نہیں ہے کہ مختلف فیہ مسائل میں سے راجح اور مرجوح اقوال کو پہچاننا اور قوت وضعف کے اعتبار سے ان اقوال کے درجات کو جاننا علم کے حصول میں کوشش کرنے والوں کی آخری آرزو ہوا کرتی ہے، لہذا! مفتی اور قاضی پر فرض ہے کہ وہ تحقیقی جواب دیں، اندازے سے جواب نہ دیں، حلال کو حرام کر کے یا حرام کو حلال کر کے اللہ تعالی پر افتراء سے ڈرے، اس کے لئے نفسانی خواہش کی اتباع کرنا اور اس مال کی طرف مائل ہونا حرام ہے جو بڑی آفت اور عظیم مصیبت ہے، اس لیے کہ فتوی دینا نازک کام ہے، اس سلسلہ میں ناواقف اور بد بخت لوگ ہی جسارت کرتے ہیں۔ (شرح عقود رسم المفتی: ٥٤) علامہ شامی کی مایہ ناز کتاب شرح عقود رسم المفتی کے اکثر مضامین میں انھیں اصول وضوابط کوتحریر کیا گیا ہے جن کی بنیاد پر راج و مرجوح اقوال میں تمیز کیا جاتا ہے اور جن کی بنیاد پر مشائخ کی ترجیحات میں تطبیق دی جاتی ہے، فقیہ العصر مولانا خالد سیف اللہ رحمانی نے بھی کتاب الفتاوی کے مقدمہ میں ان اسباب کی جانب اختصار کے ساتھ اشارہ کیا ہے جن کی بنیاد پر متعارض اقوال میں سے کسی قول کو راجح قرار دیا جاتا ہے اور ترجیح میں اختلاف کی صورت میں کسی ایک فقیہ کی ترجیح پر عمل کر لیا جاتا ہے، مولانا فرماتے ہیں کہ جن مسائل میں مشائخ حنفیہ کے مابین اختلاف رائے پایا جاتا ہے ان میں ترجیح کی بنیادیں کیا ہوں گی اس سلسلہ میں مختلف اسباب و وجوہ کا تذکرہ کیا گیا ہے جن کا خلاصہ درج ذیل ہے:
۱۔ بسا اوقات شخصیت کی بنیاد پر ترجیح دی جاتی ہے، مثلاً جو فقیہ اونچے طبقہ میں شامل ہوتا ہے اس کا قول اس فقیہ کے مقابلے میں رائج ہوتا ہے جو اس سے نچلے طبقہ میں ہوتا ہے۔
۲۔ کبھی ترجیح نقل و روایت کے استناد کے اعتبار سے دی جاتی ہے، یعنی ایک مسئلہ میں دو اختلافی اقوال سامنے آنے کی صورت میں اس قول کو راجح سمجھا جاتا ہے جو مضبوط سند سے مروی ہوتا ہے، مثلاً ظاہر الروایہ اور روایۃ النوادر میں تعارض کی صورت میں ظاہر الروایہ کا قول راجح ہوتا ہے۔
۳۔ بعض مرتبہ کتابوں کی بنیاد پر ترجیح دی جاتی ہے، اس لیے کہ بعض مصنفین مذہب کی معتبر روایات کو نقل کرنے کا اہتمام کرتے ہیں اور بعض اہل علم ہر طرح کے اقوال جمع کر دیتے ہیں، مثلاً متون اور شروح میں تعارض ہونے کی صورت میں متون والے قول کو ترجیح دی جاتی ہے، اس لیے کہ متون کا درجہ شروح سے بڑھا ہوا ہے۔
۴۔ بعض دفعہ دلیل کی بنیاد پر ترجیح دی جاتی ہے، مثلاً ایک قول استحسان پر مبنی ہو اور دوسرے قول کی بنیاد قیاس پر ہو تو عموما اس قول کو ترجیح دی جاتی ہے جو استحسان پر مبنی ہوتا ہے۔
۵۔ بسا اوقات ترجیح کی بنیاد وہ الفاظ ترجیح ہوا کرتے ہیں جن کو فقہاء کسی قول کی صحت کی طرف اشارہ کرنے کے لیے لکھا کرتے ہیں، مثلاً ایک فقیہ کسی قول کو صحیح قرار دیں اور دوسرا فقیہ اس کے مخالف قول کو اصبح قرار دیں تو جس نے اصح کا لفظ استعمال کیا ہے ان کی ترجیح معتبر ہوتی ہے۔
مستفاد از مقدمه کتاب الفتاوی: ۲۶۰/۱-۲۶۶) ذیل میں شرح عقود رسم المفتی کے پورے مضامین کو سامنے رکھتے ہوئے ترجیح کے اصول وضوابط کو قدرے تفصیل سے نقل کیا جاتا ہے۔
Second Principle: Principles of Preference Among Conflicting Rulings

Now that you have come to know that a mufti is obligated to follow only the preponderant opinion and issuing a fatwa based on the outweighed opinion is contrary to consensus, it is now necessary for you to become acquainted with the principles and rules on the basis of which one of the conflicting opinions is considered preponderant and the other outweighed. Therefore, it is stated in Fatawa Khairiyya: There is no doubt that recognizing the preponderant and outweighed opinions among disputed issues and knowing the ranks of these opinions in terms of strength and weakness is the ultimate aspiration of those striving for the acquisition of knowledge. Hence, it is obligatory upon the mufti and the judge to give an investigated answer, not a speculative one. They should fear fabricating against Allah by declaring something lawful as unlawful or unlawful as lawful. Following one's desires and inclining towards wealth is forbidden, as it is a great calamity and immense tribulation, because issuing fatwas is a delicate matter; only the ignorant and unfortunate dare to engage in it. (Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 54)

In most of the contents of Allama Shami's magnum opus, Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti, those principles and rules have been written on the basis of which preponderant and outweighed opinions are distinguished and on the basis of which reconciliation is made among the preferences of the scholars. The jurist of the age, Maulana Khalid Saifullah Rahmani, has also briefly pointed out in the introduction of Kitab al-Fatawa the causes on the basis of which an opinion among conflicting opinions is deemed preponderant and, in case of difference in preference, one scholar's preference is acted upon. Maulana states: Regarding the issues in which there is difference of opinion among the Hanafi scholars, what are the bases of preference? In this regard, various causes and reasons have been mentioned, whose summary is as follows:

1. Sometimes preference is given on the basis of personality, for example, the opinion of a jurist who belongs to a higher stratum prevails over one from a lower stratum.
2. Sometimes preference is given based on the authority of transmission and narration; that is, when two conflicting opinions appear on an issue, the opinion transmitted with a stronger chain is considered preponderant. For example, when Zahir al-Riwayah and Riwayat al-Nawadir conflict, the opinion of Zahir al-Riwayah is preponderant.
3. Sometimes preference is given on the basis of books, because some authors take care to transmit reliable narrations of the madhhab, while other scholars collect all kinds of opinions. For example, when matn and sharh conflict, the opinion of the matn is given preference, because the rank of matun is higher than that of shuruh.
4. Sometimes preference is given on the basis of evidence; for example, if one opinion is based on istihsan and the other on qiyas, generally the opinion based on istihsan is given preference.
5. Sometimes the basis of preference is the words of preference that jurists write to indicate the correctness of an opinion. For example, if one jurist declares an opinion as sahih and another jurist declares the opposing opinion as asbah, then the preference of the one who used the word asahh is considered reliable.

(Taken from Muqaddima Kitab al-Fatawa: 1/260-266)

Below, keeping all the contents of Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti in view, the principles and regulations of preference are transmitted in somewhat more detail.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage is a methodological introduction to the principles of preference (tarjih) among conflicting rulings within the Hanafi madhhab. It begins by emphasizing the mufti's obligation to follow only the preponderant opinion, citing Fatawa Khairiyya that distinguishing antara rajih and marjuh is a critical skill. The author then notes that Allama Shami's Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti largely addresses these principles. The core of the passage is a summary of five bases for tarjih, as compiled by Maulana Khalid Saifullah Rahmani in his Muqaddima to Kitab al-Fatawa. First, personality: the opinion of a higher-ranking jurist (e.g., a mujtahid mutlaq) outweighs that of a lower one (e.g., a mujtahid murajjih). Second, transmission: narrations from Zahir al-Riwayah, the authoritative corpus of Imam Muhammad, are preferred over rare or weak narrations (Riwayat al-Nawadir). Third, book type: matn (core text) is preferred over sharh (commentary) because matn authors carefully selected reliable transmissions. Fourth, evidence: istihsan (juristic preference) outweighs qiyas (analogy) because istihsan often rests on stronger textual evidence or necessity. Fifth, wording: terms like 'asahh' (more correct) indicate the author's explicit preference, and such indications are given weight in tarjih. This lesson sets the stage for a detailed exposition of each principle in subsequent text.

Key Terms
ترجیح (tarjīḥ): The process of determining which of two conflicting rulings or opinions is stronger and should be followed.
ظاہر الروایہ (Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah): The set of six authoritative books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, considered the most reliable source of Hanafi rulings.
روایۃ النوادر (Riwāyat al-Nawādir): Rare or less widely transmitted narrations, often collected by later scholars, not part of the six authoritative books.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference that seeks a softer or more equitable outcome, often based on a stronger textual indication or public interest.
قیاس (qiyās): Legal analogy, deriving a ruling for a new case from an existing ruling due to shared effective cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which type of transmission is given preference when Zahir al-Riwayah and Riwayat al-Nawadir conflict?
A) Riwayat al-Nawadir
B) Zahir al-Riwayah
C) Both are equal
D) The one preferred by the later scholars

Key Takeaway
The five bases for tarjih—personality, transmission, book type, evidence, and wording—provide a systematic framework for the mufti to determine the preponderant opinion in the Hanafi madhhab.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

The Four Bases of Tarjih in Hanafi Fatwa
Listing the four fundamental bases of tarjih in Hanafi fatwa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four bases of tarjih in Hanafi fatwa practice and apply the hierarchy to resolve conflicting narrations.

Core Idea
Tarjih in Hanafi fatwa rests on four pillars: personality of jurist, strength of transmission, type of book, and nature of evidence.

When a mufti encounters conflicting rulings within the Hanafi madhhab, he must determine which is preferred (rajih). The classical Hanafi framework provides four bases for such preference: the rank of the jurist, the reliability of the transmission chain, the authority of the book containing the ruling, and the strength of the underlying evidence. This lesson unpacks each of these bases as formulated in the Rasm al-Mufti literature.

Guided Path
1
Understand the concept of tarjih
Tarjih is the method by which a mufti chooses between equally plausible rulings within the madhhab when conflict arises. It is a key skill in mufti training.
Tarjih is not arbitrary; it follows established principles.
2
List the four bases
Memorize the four bases: shakhsiyyah (personality), naql (transmission), kitab (book), dalil (evidence). These are the pillars of preference.
The Arabic terms are: شخصیت، نقل، کتاب، دلیل.
3
Examine internal hierarchy of each base
For each base, identify which element is preferred. For personality: higher-ranking jurist > lower-ranking. For transmission: Zahir al-Riwayah > Nawadir. For book: mutun (texts) > shuruh (commentaries). For evidence: istihsan > qiyas (generally).
These hierarchies are not absolute; they guide the mufti's judgment.
4
Recognize contextual application
The four bases may conflict. The mufti must weigh them based on the specifics of the case. Personality may sometimes override book type, etc. The passage presents them as separate considerations.
The passage states 'sometimes' each basis is used, indicating flexibility.
5
Note tarjih terminology
Jurists use specific words to indicate preference, such as 'asahh' (more correct) or 'sahih' (sound). When two jurists use different terms, the one using 'asahh' is given preference.
This is part of the 'dalil' base as well.

سلسلہ میں مختلف اسباب و وجوہ کا تذکرہ کیا گیا ہے جن کا خلاصہ درج ذیل ہے:
ا۔ بسا اوقات شخصیت کی بنیاد پر ترجیح دی جاتی ہے، مثلاً جو فقیہ اونچے طبقہ میں شامل ہوتا ہے اس کا قول اس فقیہ کے مقابلے میں رائج ہوتا ہے جو اس سے نچلے طبقہ میں ہوتا ہے۔
۲۔ کبھی ترجیح نقل و روایت کے استناد کے اعتبار سے دی جاتی ہے، یعنی ایک مسئلہ میں دو اختلافی اقوال سامنے آنے کی صورت میں اس قول کو راجح سمجھا جاتا ہے جو مضبوط سند سے مروی ہوتا ہے، مثلاً ظاہر الروایہ اور روایۃ النوادر میں تعارض کی صورت میں ظاہر الروایہ کا قول راجح ہوتا ہے۔ ۳۔ بعض مرتبہ کتابوں کی بنیاد پر ترجیح دی جاتی ہے، اس لیے کہ بعض مصنفین مذہب کی معتبر روایات کو نقل کرنے کا اہتمام کرتے ہیں اور بعض اہل علم ہر طرح کے اقوال جمع کر دیتے ہیں، مثلاً متون اور شروح میں تعارض ہونے کی صورت میں متون والے قول کو ترجیح دی جاتی ہے، اس لیے کہ متون کا درجہ شروح سے بڑھا ہوا ہے۔
-۴۔ بعض دفعہ دلیل کی بنیاد پر ترجیح دی جاتی ہے، مثلاً ایک قول استحسان پر مبنی ہو اور دوسرے قول کی بنیاد قیاس پر ہو تو عموما اس قول کو ترجیح دی جاتی ہے جو استحسان پر مبنی ہوتا ہے۔ بسا اوقات ترجیح کی بنیاد وہ الفاظ تر جیح ہوا کرتے ہیں جن کو فقہاء کسی قول کی صحت کی طرف اشارہ کرنے کے لیے لکھا کرتے ہیں، مثلاً ایک فقیہ کسی قول کو صحیح قرار دیں اور دوسرا فقیہ اس کے مخالف قول کو اصبح قرار دیں تو جس نے اصح کا لفظ استعمال کیا ہے ان کی ترجیح معتبر ہوتی ہے۔
مستفاد از مقدمه کتاب الفتاوی: ۲۶۰/۱ ۲۶۶)
ذیل میں شرح عقود رسم المفتی کے پورے مضامین کو سامنے رکھتے ہوئے ترجیح کے اصول وضوابط کو قدرے تفصیل سے نقل کیا جاتا ہے۔
Various causes and reasons have been mentioned in the series, the summary of which is as follows:
1. Sometimes preference is given on the basis of personality; for example, a jurist who belongs to a higher class, his statement is preferred over a jurist who is in a lower class.
2. Sometimes preference is given according to the authority of transmission and narration; that is, when two conflicting statements appear in a matter, the statement that is narrated with a stronger chain is considered preferable; for example, in case of conflict between Zahir al-Riwayah and Riwayat al-Nawadir, the statement of Zahir al-Riwayah is preferred.
3. Sometimes preference is given on the basis of books; because some authors strive to transmit the reliable narrations of the madhhab while some scholars collect all kinds of statements; for example, in case of conflict between texts (mutun) and commentaries (shuruh), the statement of the texts is preferred because the status of texts is higher than that of commentaries.
4. Sometimes preference is given on the basis of evidence; for example, if one statement is based on istihsan and another on qiyas, generally preference is given to the statement based on istihsan. Sometimes the basis of preference is the words of preference that jurists write to indicate the soundness of a statement; for example, if one jurist declares a statement as sahih and another declares the opposing statement as asahh, then the preference of the one who used the word asahh is considered valid.
Benefited from Muqaddima Kitab al-Fatawa: 1/260-266
Below, with the entire contents of Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti in view, the principles and rules of preference are narrated in some detail.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage introduces the four fundamental bases for tarjih (preference) within the Hanafi madhhab when conflicting narrations or opinions arise. The author, from Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti, lists these bases as principles for a mufti to determine which ruling to adopt in his fatwa. The first basis is the personality (shakhsiyyah) of the jurist: the opinion of a higher-ranking jurist, such as an Imam of the madhhab, is preferred over that of a lower-ranking jurist. The second basis is the strength of transmission (naql wa riwayah): narrations transmitted through the six core books of the madhhab (Zahir al-Riwayah) are preferred over rare transmissions (Riwayat al-Nawadir). The third basis is the type of book (kitab): primary texts (mutun) are given precedence over commentaries (shuruh) because they are considered more authoritative. The fourth basis is the nature of the evidence (dalil): rulings based on istihsan (juristic preference) are generally preferred over those based on pure qiyas (analogy). Additionally, certain terms like 'asahh' (more correct) indicate a preference by the jurist himself. This passage sets the stage for a detailed discussion of thirteen principles of tarjih based on personality, which follow later in the text.

Key Terms
ظاہر الروایہ (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani containing the authoritative transmitted rulings of the madhhab.
روایۃ النوادر (Riwayat al-Nawadir): Rare or less common transmissions from the Hanafi imams, not part of the six core books.
استحسان (Istihsan): Juristic preference based on equity or public interest, a method of reasoning in Hanafi usul.
قیاس (Qiyas): Analogical deduction from an original ruling to a new case due to shared effective cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, when there is a conflict between a statement from Zahir al-Riwayah and a statement from Riwayat al-Nawadir, which is preferred?
A) Riwayat al-Nawadir
B) Zahir al-Riwayah
C) The statement based on istihsan
D) The statement from commentaries

Key Takeaway
The four bases of tarjih provide a systematic framework for Hanafi muftis to resolve conflicting rulings, but their application requires nuanced judgment.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
beginner
6 min
First Principle of Tarjih by Personality: Single Narration is Binding
Stating the first principle of tarjih by personality: a single narration is binding.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the first principle of tarjih by personality: determine when a single Hanafi narration is binding for fatwa and when it may be set aside due to a missing cause.

Core Idea
A single opinion from the Hanafi school is binding unless its underlying cause has ceased.

Within the Hanafi madhhab, not all transmitted opinions carry equal weight. Sometimes only one narration reaches us from the early jurists. The first principle of personality-based preference (tarjih bil-shakhsiyyah) states that such a single narration must be followed, regardless of whether it comes from the authoritative Zahir al-Riwayah, the rare Nawadir, or later fatawa. However, the school is not rigid: if the cause behind the ruling is clearly absent, the ruling itself may be abandoned. This lesson anchors that rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source of the narration
Determine whether the single narration originates from Zahir al-Riwayah, Nawadir, or later fatawa/waqi'at. The principle applies equally to all, so classification does not change the default binding nature.
Zahir al-Riwayah carries the highest authority, but for this principle, all sources are treated the same unless the cause is absent.
2
Verify that it is the only narration
Confirm that no other Hanafi opinion exists on the matter. The principle only activates when there is a single transmitted opinion from the Hanafi school.
If multiple narrations exist, other tarjih principles (e.g., by number, by strength of proof) apply.
3
Check for the existence of the underlying cause
Investigate whether the ruling was based on a specific cause (illah) that may no longer exist. If it is intuitively known (badihan) that the illah is absent, the ruling is no longer binding.
This exception prevents outdated rulings from being applied when circumstances have fundamentally changed.
4
Issue the fatwa accordingly
If the cause remains, give fatwa according to the single narration. If the cause is absent, you are free to adopt a different opinion (from another school or ijtihad) as long as it aligns with Hanafi principles.
The mufti must document the reason for departing from the transmitted opinion.

Source Text

شخصیت کی بنیاد پر ترجیح کے تیرہ (۱۳) اصول
فقہ حنفی کے مختلف فیہ اقوال میں سے کسی قول کو بعض اوقات شخصیت کی بنیاد پر ترجیح دی جاتی ہے، کیوں کہ علمی اور تحقیقی اعتبار سے تمام فقہاء یکساں صفات کے حامل نہیں ہوتے ہیں ، ان میں فقہی بصیرت اور دلائل کی معرفت کے اعتبار سے نمایاں فرق ہوتا ہے، لہذا جو فقیہ علم وتحقیق میں بڑھا ہوا ہو اس کا قول اپنے مقابل کی بہ نسبت زیادہ راجح ہوگا، نیز ایسا بھی ہوتا ہے کہ ایک فقیہ کو بسا اوقات ممارست اور تجربہ کی بنیاد پر فقہ کے مختلف ابواب میں سے کسی مخصوص باب میں زیادہ مہارت ہو جاتی ہے، جب کہ اس باب میں دوسرے فقیہ کو اتنی مہارت نہیں ہوتی ہے، لہذا ایسی صورت میں اس باب کے ماہر مفتی کے قول کو دوسرے فقیہ کے قول پر مقدم کرنالازم ہوگا، اسی طرح کبھی کبھی کسی مسئلہ میں احناف کے ائمہ ثلاثہ کا اتفاق ہونے کے باوجود متاخرین فقہاء کا اس مسئلہ میں اختلاف ہو جاتا ہے، لہذا ان تمام صورتوں میں فتوی دیتے وقت درج ذیل اصولوں کی پابندی ضروری ہوگی:
پہلا اصول : جب احناف سے صرف ایک قول مروی ہو جب کسی مسئلہ میں فقہاء احناف سے صرف ایک قول مروی ہو تو اسی قول پر عمل کرنا اور فتوی دینا لازم ہے، خواہ وہ مسئلہ ظاہر الروایہ سے ماخوذ ہو یا نوادر سے یا فتاوی و واقعات سے لیکن اگر بدیہی طور پر یہ معلوم ہو جائے کہ اس مسئلہ کا جواب کسی ایسی علت پر مبنی تھا جو علت اب نہیں پائی جارہی ہے تو اس قول پر عمل کرنا لازم نہ ہو گا۔
اصول الافتاء و آدابه : ۱۹۸ ، المدخل المفصل الى الفقه الحنفي لابي الحاج: ٥٢٣)
Thirteen principles of preference on the basis of personality:
Sometimes, among the disputed statements of Hanafi fiqh, preference is given to a statement on the basis of personality, because all jurists are not equal in knowledge and research; there is a significant difference among them in terms of juristic insight and knowledge of proofs. Therefore, the statement of a jurist who is advanced in knowledge and research will be more preferable compared to his counterpart. Also, it sometimes happens that a jurist, due to practice and experience, becomes more expert in a particular chapter among the various chapters of fiqh, while another jurist does not have as much expertise in that chapter. Hence, in such a situation, it is necessary to prefer the statement of the expert mufti in that chapter over the statement of another jurist. Similarly, sometimes in a matter, despite the agreement of the three Imams of the Hanafis, later jurists differ on that matter. Therefore, while giving fatwa in all these situations, compliance with the following principles is necessary:
First principle: When only one statement is narrated from the Hanafis - if only one statement is transmitted from the Hanafi jurists in a particular matter, then it is necessary to act upon that very statement and give fatwa accordingly, whether that matter is taken from Zahir al-Riwayah or from Nawadir or from Fatawa and Waqi'at. But if it becomes intuitively known that the answer to this matter was based on a certain cause (illah) which is no longer found, then it will not be necessary to act upon that statement.
[Source: Usul al-Ifta' wa Adabuhu: 198, al-Mudkhal al-Mufassal ila al-Fiqh al-Hanafi by Abi al-Hajj: 523]
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is part of a larger section in Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti discussing the thirteen principles of tarjih (preference) based on personality (shakhsiyyah) within the Hanafi madhhab. The author first provides a preamble explaining why personality matters: not all Hanafi jurists are equal in knowledge, insight, and expertise. Some are more advanced in research, and some specialize in particular areas of fiqh. Even when the earlier three Imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Imam Muhammad) are unanimous, later jurists may differ. In all such cases, the personality-based principles apply. The first principle is presented: when only a single opinion is transmitted from Hanafi jurists on a matter, that opinion must be followed and fatwa must be given according to it, regardless of whether it originates from the authoritative Zahir al-Riwayah texts, the rare Nawadir narrations, or later fatawa and waqi'at (occurrences). The only exception is if it becomes intuitively clear (badihan) that the ruling was based on a particular cause ('illah) that no longer exists. In that case, the ruling is abandoned because its effective cause has ceased, aligning with the principle that rulings change with changing customs and conditions. This shows the dynamic nature of Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
ظاہر الروایہ (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani containing the authoritative transmitted rulings of the madhhab.
نوادر (Nawadir): Rare transmissions from the Hanafi imams, not part of the six core books.
علت (‘Illah): The effective cause or ratio legis behind a ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first principle of tarjih by personality, what must a mufti do if only one narration is transmitted from Hanafi jurists on a matter, and it is from the Nawadir?
A) He may choose to follow it or not based on his own reasoning.
B) He must follow it unless the underlying cause is no longer present.
C) He must reject it because it is not from Zahir al-Riwayah.
D) He must compare it with qiyas before issuing a fatwa.

Key Takeaway
When only one Hanafi opinion exists, it is binding for fatwa unless its cause is clearly absent.

Personality-Based Preference in Hanafi Fatwa
Introduction to the basis and scenarios for personality-based preference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the rationale for personality-based preference (tarjīḥ bi al-shakhṣiyyah) in Hanafi iftāʾ and identify the three scenarios where it applies.

Core Idea
A mufti gives precedence to a more knowledgeable jurist or a chapter expert, even over the three imams' agreement in some cases.

This passage lays the foundation for the thirteen principles of personality-based preference. Not all Hanafi jurists are equal in knowledge, insight, or specialization. When evidence is balanced or unclear, the mufti must weigh the jurist's personal authority. This introductory lesson explains why personality matters in fatwa and previews the need for systematic rules.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the problem: diversity of jurists
The passage notes that Hanafi jurists are not uniform in scholarly depth, knowledge of proofs, or fiqh insight. This variation creates the need for a method to choose among their views.
This is a reality of the madhhab's development, not a judgment on any jurist's competence.
2
Identify the first basis: general superiority
A jurist who excels overall in knowledge and research deserves preference over a lesser contemporary or later jurist, all else being equal.
This is a straightforward application: the more learned person's view is more reliable.
3
Identify the second basis: chapter specialization
A jurist may develop exceptional expertise in one chapter of fiqh through practice and experience. In that chapter, his view is preferred over a generalist or a jurist weaker in that area.
This recognizes that competence can be domain-specific.
4
Identify the third basis: later jurists' disagreement after consensus of the three imams
Even when the three leading imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) agree, later Hanafi jurists may still differ. The mufti must apply personality-based principles to decide which later view carries weight.
This scenario shows that personality-based preference also applies when the foundation is already settled by the early masters.
5
Connect to the upcoming principles
The passage concludes that all these situations require adherence to thirteen specific principles, which will be detailed in subsequent lessons.
Your task now is to internalize the rationale so that the principles become meaningful.

Among the differing views of the Hanafi school, sometimes preference is given based on personality, because not all jurists possess equal attributes in terms of knowledge and research; there is a noticeable difference among them in fiqh insight and knowledge of proofs. Therefore, the statement of a jurist who excels in knowledge and research will be more preponderant compared to his counterpart. In such a case, it is necessary to give precedence to the statement of the expert mufti in that chapter over the statement of the other jurist. Similarly, sometimes despite the agreement of the three leading Hanafi imams on an issue, later jurists differ on that issue. Commentary
This passage introduces the concept of personality-based preference (tarjīḥ bi al-shakhṣiyyah). The author explains that not all Hanafi jurists are equal in scholarly depth, expertise in proofs, or specialization in specific areas of fiqh. Therefore, when multiple views exist, the view of a more knowledgeable jurist or a specialist in the relevant chapter is given precedence. Additionally, even when the three leading imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) agree, later jurists may still differ, and that situation requires careful handling. This sets the stage for the thirteen principles that follow.

Key Terms
شخصیت کی بنیاد پر ترجیح (shakhṣiyyat kī bunyād par tarjīḥ): Preferencing one jurist's view over another based on the jurist's scholarly rank, expertise, or specialization.
ائمہ ثلاثہ (aʾimmat al-thalātha): The three leading imams of the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

The First Principle: Acting on a Single Narration
Principle for acting on a single narration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the first principle of Hanafi fatwa hierarchy to determine when a mufti must follow a single narrated opinion.

Core Idea
A single narrated Hanafi view is binding unless its underlying cause ('illah) is obviously absent.

In the Hanafi school, the mufti must know which opinions are authoritative. The first principle of Rasm al-Mufti provides a clear rule: when only one opinion is reported from the Hanafi jurists on a matter, it must be adopted for fatwa, regardless of its source layer — whether from the well-known Zahir al-Riwayah, the rarer Nawadir, or later Fatawa. However, this principle is not absolute. It includes an exception based on legal cause ('illah) that allows departure from the ruling when the cause no longer applies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the narration source
Determine whether the single opinion comes from Zahir al-Riwayah, Nawadir, or later Fatawa. This affects the hierarchy but not the initial obligation to follow it under this principle.
All sources are treated equally under this rule; the level only matters if multiple narrations exist.
2
Confirm singularity
Ensure that no other contradictory Hanafi narration exists on the same matter. If there is more than one, other principles (e.g., preference for Zahir al-Riwayah) apply.
This principle is only triggered when the school speaks with one voice.
3
Assess the continued existence of the 'illah
Examine the ruling's underlying cause. If it is intuitively clear that the cause no longer exists, the ruling is not binding. This requires understanding the ratio legis (ta'lil) and current circumstances.
The exception is based on 'badihatan' (evident knowledge), not speculative assessment.
4
Formulate the fatwa
If the cause is still present, issue the fatwa based on the single narration. If the cause is absent, you may (or must) depart from it, often reverting to a more appropriate ruling from the school's broader treasury.
In practice, consulting later fatwa compilations or senior muftis is recommended when departing.

Source Text

پہلا اصول : جب احناف سے صرف ایک قول مروی ہو جب کسی مسئلہ میں فقہاء احناف سے صرف ایک قول مروی ہو تو اسی قول پر عمل کرنا اور فتوی دینا لازم ہے، خواہ وہ مسئلہ ظاہر الروایہ سے ماخوذ ہو یا نوادر سے یا فتاوی و واقعات سے لیکن اگر بدیہی طور پر یہ معلوم ہو جائے کہ اس مسئلہ کا جواب کسی ایسی علت پر مبنی تھا جو علت اب نہیں پائی جارہی ہے تو اس قول پر عمل کرنا لازم نہ ہو گا۔
First principle: When only one view is narrated from the Hanafis. When only one view is narrated from the Hanafi jurists on a matter, it is necessary to act upon that view and give fatwa accordingly, whether that matter is taken from Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah or from Nawādir or from Fatāwā and Wāqiʿāt. But if it becomes evident intuitively that the answer to this matter was based on a cause (ʿillah) that is no longer present, then acting upon that view is not necessary.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This is a memorization rule. The first principle states that when only a single opinion is transmitted from the Hanafi school on a matter, the mufti must adopt it and give fatwa accordingly, regardless of the source's hierarchy (Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah, Nawādir, or later fatāwā). However, there is an exception: if it is obvious that the ruling was based on a specific cause that no longer exists, then adherence is not required. This safeguards against blindly following a ruling that has become obsolete due to changing circumstances.

Key Terms
ظاہر الروایہ (Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah): The transmitted opinions from Imam Muhammad's six well-known books; the most authoritative layer of Hanafi rulings.
نوادر (Nawādir): Rare or solitary transmissions from Hanafi imams, not found in the six major books.
علت (ʿillah): The effective cause or ratio legis behind a ruling, which may change over time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first principle, when is a mufti NOT required to follow a single Hanafi narration?
A) When the narration comes from Nawādir
B) When the narration comes from later fatāwā
C) When it is intuitively clear that the cause ('illah) for the ruling no longer exists
D) When the narration contradicts the view of the Ṣāḥibayn

Key Takeaway
A mufti must follow a single Hanafi narration unless its foundational cause is clearly obsolete.

Second Principle: Fatwa on Imam Abu Hanifa's View Alone
Stating that Imam Abu Hanifa's solitary view is followed without need for later tarjih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the second principle of rasm al-mufti concerning Imam Abu Hanifa's solitary view and apply it to determine when a fatwa can be given without later tarjih.

Core Idea
Imam Abu Hanifa's solitary view is inherently authoritative; no later tarjih is needed.

This lesson focuses on a foundational rule in Hanafi fatwa methodology: when only Imam Abu Hanifa's solitary view exists on a matter, it is followed directly. Later scholars' explicit validation is not required. This principle, quoted from Ibn Bujaym, emphasizes the Imam's supreme authority and simplifies the mufti's task.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source of the rule
Locate the statement from Ibn Bujaym that establishes the principle: the Imam's view does not need preference or validation from later shaykhs.
This rule is part of the rasm al-mufti genre, which guides muftis on which opinions to adopt.
2
Understand the scope
The rule applies when only Imam Abu Hanifa's view is transmitted for a given issue. If multiple views exist, tarjih may be needed.
The solitude of the view must be verified through reliable Hanafi sources.
3
Apply the principle
When the condition is met, the mufti gives fatwa on the Imam's view without requiring later endorsement. The ruling is considered binding.
This simplifies the mufti's work: no need to search for later tarjih.
4
Differentiate from other rules
Contrast this with cases involving the Ṣāḥibayn or later mujtahids, where tarjih among multiple valid opinions may be necessary.
The Imam's unique rank justifies this exception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دوسرا اصول: امام اعظم کے قول پر فتوی دینا جب کسی مسئلہ میں صرف امام ابوحنیفہ کا قول منقول ہو تو اسی پر فتوی دیں گے، خواہ علماء مذہب میں سے کسی فقیہ نے اس قول کی تصحیح وترجیح کی صراحت کی ہو یا نہیں، علامہ ابن بجیم فرماتے ہیں: امام ابوحنیفہ کے قول کو مشائخ مذہب کی ترجیح وتصیح کی ضرورت نہیں ہے، لہذا جب کسی مسئلہ میں ان کا قول پایا جائے تو اسی پر عمل کیا جائے گا، خواہ مشائخ نے اس کی صحت کی صراحت کی ہو یا نہ کی ہو۔
Second principle: Giving fatwa on the view of Imam al-Aʿẓam. When only the view of Imam Abu Hanifa is transmitted on a matter, we will give fatwa on it, whether or not any jurist among the scholars of the school explicitly declared its validity and preference. ʿAllāmah Ibn Bujaym says: 'The view of Imam Abu Hanifa does not need the preference and validation of the shaykhs of the school. Therefore, whenever his view is found on a matter, it will be acted upon, whether the shaykhs explicitly declared its authenticity or not.'
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This rule affirms the preeminence of Imam Abu Hanifa's ijtihad. When only his opinion is recorded, it is automatically binding; later scholars' tarjih is unnecessary. The quote from Ibn Bujaym reinforces that the Imam's view is inherently authoritative and does not depend on the endorsement of later shaykhs. This principle underscores the foundational status of the Imam's ijtihad within the school.

Key Terms
امام اعظم (al-Imām al-Aʿẓam): The Greatest Imam, a title for Abu Hanifa (d. 150 AH).
تصحیح وترجیح (taṣḥīḥ wa tarjīḥ): The process of declaring a view correct and giving it preference over others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Confirmation from the Ṣāḥibayn
C) No additional endorsement is needed; his view is intrinsically authoritative
D) It must be from Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah

Key Takeaway
Imam Abu Hanifa's solitary view is followed directly without need for later tarjih.

Third Principle: Follow the Preferred View Among Multiple Narrations
Rasm al-Mufti principle 3: following aṣḥāb al-tarjīḥ.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the third principle of Rasm al-Mufti to identify which view a mufti must follow when multiple Hanafi narrations exist.

Core Idea
When Hanafi views conflict, the mufti follows the later scholars' preference, not his own.

This lesson establishes a foundational rule for muftis: when multiple narrations from Hanafi imams exist on a single issue, the mufti does not choose arbitrarily. Instead, he must defer to the scholars of tarjīḥ (aṣḥāb al-tarjīḥ) — later authorities who mastered the proofs of both Imam Abu Hanifa and his companions. Their preference is binding, even if they chose the view of the Ṣāḥibayn over that of Abu Hanifa himself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the situation
Determine that there are multiple transmitted views from Hanafi imams on a single ruling.
2
Recall the principle
State the rule: The mufti must follow the view preferred by aṣḥāb al-tarjīḥ.
This is a binding rule, not advisory.
3
Understand the justification
The aṣḥāb al-tarjīḥ were fully aware of the proofs of both sides; therefore, their tarjīḥ is reliable.
They dedicated their works to supporting and refining the school.
4
Apply the rule
In a fatwa, identify which view the aṣḥāb al-tarjīḥ have preferred and issue fatwa accordingly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تیسرا اصول : جب احناف سے مختلف اقوال مروی ہوں جب کسی مسئلہ میں فقہاء احناف سے مختلف اقوال مروی ہوں تو مفتی اس قول پر فتوی دے گا جس کو علماء مذہب میں سے اصحاب الترجیح نے راجح قرار دیا ہو، خواہ ان حضرات نے امام اعظم کے قول کو ترجیح دی ہو یا صاحبین کے قول کو ، کیوں کہ یہ حضرات امام اعظم اور صاحبین دونوں کے دلائل سے واقف تھے، ان کے بارے میں یہ گمان نہیں کیا جاسکتا کہ انھوں نے امام اعظم کے قول کو چھوڑ کر صاحبین کے قول پر اس لئے فتوی دیا کہ وہ امام صاحب کی دلیل پر مطلع نہیں ہو سکے، کیوں کہ ہم دیکھتے ہیں کہ انھوں نے اپنی کتابوں کو دونوں کے دلائل سے بھر دیا اور وقت ہے اور انھوں نے اپنے آپ کو مذہب حنفی کی تائید و تنقیح کے لئے وقف کر دیا تھا، پس ان کی ترجیح پر عمل کرنا واجب ہوگا، خواہ وہ کسی بھی فقیہ کے قول کو راجح قرار دیں۔
Third principle: When different views are narrated from the Hanafis. When different views are narrated from the Hanafi jurists on a matter, the mufti will give fatwa on the view that the people of preference (aṣḥāb al-tarjīḥ) among the scholars of the school have declared preponderant, whether those gentlemen preferred the view of Imam al-Aʿẓam or the view of the Ṣāḥibayn. Because they were acquainted with the proofs of both Imam al-Aʿẓam and the Ṣāḥibayn. It cannot be conjectured that they gave fatwa on the Ṣāḥibayn's view while abandoning the Imam's view because they could not access the Imam's proof. We see that they filled their books with the proofs of both and dedicated their time to supporting and refining the Hanafi school. Therefore, acting upon their preference is obligatory, regardless of whose view they declare preponderant.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
The third principle addresses the common situation of multiple transmitted views. The mufti must defer to the later authoritative scholars (aṣḥāb al-tarjīḥ, such as al-Marghīnānī, al-Kāsānī, etc.) who specialized in weighing evidence. Their choice is trusted because they had full access to the proofs of both Imam Abu Hanifa and the Ṣāḥibayn. The passage rebuts any suspicion that they might have chosen a view out of ignorance. Their thorough knowledge and dedication to the school make their tarjīḥ binding.

Key Terms
اصحاب الترجيح (aṣḥāb al-tarjīḥ): The later authoritative Hanafi scholars who wrote books of tarjīḥ, weighing the evidence from the founding imams.
صاحبین (al-Ṣāḥibayn): The two companions of Imam Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the preference of the aṣḥāb al-tarjīḥ considered binding according to the third principle?
A) Because they lived closer to the time of the founding imams
B) Because they were acquainted with the proofs of both Imam Abu Hanifa and the Ṣāḥibayn
C) Because they were appointed by the caliph
D) Because they always prefer the easier opinion

Key Takeaway
The mufti must follow the view preferred by aṣḥāb al-tarjīḥ when multiple Hanafi narrations exist, because their command of evidence makes their preference authoritative.

Obligation to Follow the Consensus of the Three Imams
Stating the binding nature of the three imams' consensus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that the agreement of the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) is binding on all muftis, regardless of their ijtihad level, and justify why departure is impermissible.

Core Idea
When the three imams agree, their ruling is irrebuttable — no later ijtihad can override it.

This fourth principle establishes a foundational rule in Hanafi fatwa methodology: the collective agreement (ittifāq) of the three founding imams—Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani—creates an absolute obligation. Even a later mujtahid within the school cannot contradict this agreement because the founders' combined ijtihad is considered superior due to their proximity to revelation, exhaustive knowledge, and access to proofs that later scholars may not fully grasp. Understanding this principle is crucial for any mufti working within the Hanafi tradition, as it defines the boundaries of valid ikhtilaf and ensures school coherence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
چوتھا اصول : جب کسی مسئلہ میں احناف کا اتفاق ہو جب کسی مسئلہ میں احناف کے ائمہ ثلاثہ یعنی امام ابوحنیفہ، امام ابو یوسف اور امام محمد کا اتفاق ہو تو انھیں کے قول پر عمل کرنا اور فتوی دینا واجب ہے،خواہ مفتی مجہتد ہو یا غیر مجتہد، کیوں کہ بعد کے کسی بھی مجتہد کا اجتہاد ان ائمہ کے اجتہاد سے قوی نہیں ہوسکتا اور نہ ہی بعد کے کسی مجتہد کی نظر متقدمین ائمہ کی نظر سے باریک ہوسکتی ہے، لہذا ظاہر بات یہ ہے کہ انھوں نے اپنے قول کی بنیاد کسی ایسی دلیل پر رکھی ہوگی جہاں تک بعد والے مجتہد مفتی کی رسائی نہیں ہوسکی، پس ائمہ ثلاثہ کے قول سے عدول کرنا جائز نہیں ہوگا۔
Fourth principle: When there is agreement of the Hanafis on a matter. When the three leading imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) agree on a matter, then acting upon their view and giving fatwa is obligatory, whether the mufti is a mujtahid or a non-mujtahid. Because the ijtihad of any later mujtahid cannot be stronger than the ijtihad of these imams, nor can the insight of any later mujtahid be more subtle than the insight of the earlier imams. Therefore, it is obvious that they based their view on a proof to which later mujtahid muftis could not have access. Hence, departing from the view of the three imams is not permissible.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
The fourth principle establishes that the unanimous agreement (ittiḥād) of the three founding imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) creates an irrebuttable ruling. Even a later mujtahid within the school cannot contradict it, because the founders' combined ijtihad is inherently superior due to their proximity to the sources and their comprehensive knowledge. The implication is that their agreement likely rests on evidence that later scholars cannot fully grasp. Therefore, the mufti, regardless of his own level, must follow their joint view without deviation.

Key Terms
اتفاق (ittifāq): The agreement of the three leading Hanafi imams on a legal ruling.
متقدمین (mutaqaddimīn): The early Hanafi authorities, especially the three imams.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because later scholars lack the time to research
B) Because the imams' ijtihad is based on evidence inaccessible to later scholars
C) Because it is a sin to disagree with any early scholar
D) Because the three imams always gave the easiest ruling

Key Takeaway
The consensus of the three Hanafi founding imams is absolutely binding and cannot be overturned by any later ijtihad.

Third Principle: Following the Rajih Saying
States the rule for preferring the rajih saying among Hanafi scholars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the third principle of fatwa by identifying which narration to follow when multiple Hanafi narrations exist.

Core Idea
The mufti must follow the saying deemed rajih by ashab al-tarjih, regardless of which Hanafi imam it originates from.

In the Hanafi madhhab, multiple rulings may be narrated from different imams. This lesson explains the third foundational principle of fatwa: when such ikhtilaf exists, the mufti does not choose arbitrarily but follows the ruling that the scholars of tarjih have determined as preponderant (rajih). This principle ensures consistency and authority in fatwa issuance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize that multiple different sayings from Hanafi jurists exist on one issue.
2
Recognize the authority
Understand that ashab al-tarjih are the qualified scholars within the madhhab to determine the preponderant opinion.
3
Follow their determination
The mufti must adopt the rajih saying, whether it is from Imam Abu Hanifah or the Sahibayn.
4
Understand the rationale
These scholars were fully aware of the proofs of all imams and dedicated to the madhhab; their tarjih is authoritative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تیسرا اصول : جب احناف سے مختلف اقوال مروی ہوں
جب کسی مسئلہ میں فقہاء احناف سے مختلف اقوال مروی ہوں تو مفتی اس قول پر فتوی دے گا جس کو علماء مذہب میں سے اصحاب الترجیح نے راجح قرار دیا ہو، خواہ ان حضرات نے امام اعظم کے قول کو ترجیح دی ہو یا صاحبین کے قول کو ، کیوں کہ یہ حضرات امام اعظم اور صاحبین دونوں کے دلائل سے واقف تھے، ان کے بارے میں یہ گمان نہیں کیا جاسکتا کہ انھوں نے امام اعظم کے قول کو چھوڑ کر صاحبین کے قول پر اس لئے فتوی دیا کہ وہ امام صاحب کی دلیل پر مطلع نہیں ہو سکے، کیوں کہ ہم دیکھتے ہیں کہ انھوں نے اپنی کتابوں کو دونوں کے دلائل سے بھر دیا اور وقت ہے اور انھوں نے اپنے آپ کو مذہب حنفی کی تائید و تنقیح کے لئے وقف کر دیا تھا، پس ان کی ترجیح پر عمل کرنا واجب ہوگا، خواہ وہ کسی بھی فقیہ کے قول کو راجح قرار دیں۔ (شرح عقود رسم المفتى: ۱۱۰،۱۰٦،٨٧)
Third Principle: When different sayings are narrated from the Hanafis. When in a matter different sayings are narrated from the Hanafi jurists, the mufti will give fatwa on that saying which the scholars of tarjih among the scholars of the madhhab have deemed preponderant, whether those scholars gave preference to the saying of Imam A'zam or to the saying of the two companions (Sahibayn). Because these scholars were aware of the proofs of both Imam A'zam and the two companions; it cannot be assumed about them that they gave fatwa on the saying of the companions abandoning the saying of Imam A'zam because they were unable to access the proof of Imam Sahib. For we see that they filled their books with the proofs of both, and they had dedicated themselves to the support and refinement of the Hanafi madhhab. So acting upon their tarjih will be obligatory, regardless of whose saying they deem preponderant. (Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 110, 106, 87)
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage presents the third principle of fatwa in the Hanafi madhhab. It addresses the situation where multiple conflicting narrations exist from Hanafi jurists on a single issue. The mufti is not free to choose arbitrarily; he must follow the ruling that the scholars of tarjih (those qualified to determine the preponderant position within the madhhab) have classified as rajih. This holds true whether those scholars preferred the view of Imam Abu Hanifah himself or the view of his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The rationale is that these later scholars were thoroughly familiar with the evidences of both imams; they did not abandon Imam Abu Hanifah's view out of ignorance of his proofs. Their dedication to the madhhab is evident in their works. Therefore, the mufti must adhere to their tarjih.

Key Terms
اصحاب الترجیح (ashab al-tarjih): Scholars within the Hanafi madhhab who have the authority to determine which of the multiple narrations is the preponderant (rajih) position.
راجح (rajih): The legal opinion that is considered stronger and more authoritative based on evidence and scholarly consensus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When there are multiple conflicting narrations from Hanafi jurists, which saying should the mufti follow?
A) The saying of Imam Abu Hanifah.
B) The saying of the Sahibayn.
C) The saying deemed rajih by the scholars of tarjih.
D) The saying most recent in time.

Key Takeaway
The third principle of fatwa: follow the rajih, not the person.

Fourth Principle: Agreement of the Three Imams
Explains the binding authority of the consensus of the three imams.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the fourth principle of Rasm al-Mufti, identifying when a ruling is binding due to the consensus of the three founding Hanafi imams.

Core Idea
When the three imams agree, their ruling is binding on all muftis, regardless of ijtihad.

This lesson introduces a key rule from the Hanafi mufti's handbook: the binding authority of the collective opinion of Imam Abu Hanifah, Imam Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. Understanding this principle is essential for any mufti or student of Hanafi fiqh, as it establishes the hierarchy of authority and prevents arbitrary departures from established positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle
Read the passage and state the principle in your own words: When do the three imams' rulings become binding?
The principle applies to all matters, not only specific chapters.
2
Understand the scope
Note that the principle applies whether the mufti is a mujtahid or not. There is no exemption for a qualified mujtahid to override the consensus.
This sets the Hanafi school apart from others that allow later ijtihad to overturn earlier positions.
3
Grasp the rationale
The passage provides two reasons: (1) later ijtihad cannot be stronger than that of the early imams, and (2) the early imams likely had access to a proof that later scholars cannot reach.
This rationale emphasizes the superiority of early jurists' insight and evidence.
4
Apply the principle
Imagine a mufti encounters a case where the three imams are known to have held the same view. According to this principle, he must give fatwa based on that view, even if he personally finds another opinion more convincing.
This ensures consistency and stability in fatwa practice.

چوتھا اصول : جب کسی مسئلہ میں احناف کا اتفاق ہو
جب کسی مسئلہ میں احناف کے ائمہ ثلاثہ یعنی امام ابوحنیفہ، امام ابو یوسف اور امام محمد کا اتفاق ہو تو انھیں کے قول پر عمل کرنا اور فتوی دینا واجب ہے،خواہ مفتی مجہتد ہو یا غیر مجتہد، کیوں کہ بعد کے کسی بھی مجتہد کا اجتہاد ان ائمہ کے اجتہاد سے قوی نہیں ہوسکتا اور نہ ہی بعد کے کسی مجتہد کی نظر متقدمین ائمہ کی نظر سے باریک ہوسکتی ہے، لہذا ظاہر بات یہ ہے کہ انھوں نے اپنے قول کی بنیاد کسی ایسی دلیل پر رکھی ہوگی جہاں تک بعد والے مجتہد مفتی کی رسائی نہیں ہوسکی، پس ائمہ ثلاثہ کے قول سے عدول کرنا جائز نہیں ہوگا۔
(شرح عقود رسم المفتى: ٩٩،٩٥)
Fourth Principle: When there is agreement of the Hanafis. When in a matter the three imams of the Hanafis, namely Imam Abu Hanifah, Imam Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad, are agreed, then acting upon their saying and giving fatwa is obligatory, whether the mufti is a mujtahid or not. Because the ijtihad of any later mujtahid cannot be stronger than the ijtihad of these imams, nor can the insight of any later mujtahid be more subtle than the insight of the early imams. So it is apparent that they based their saying on a proof that later mujtahid muftis cannot reach. Therefore, abandoning the saying of the three imams will not be permissible. (Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 99, 95)
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This fourth principle addresses the situation when all three early authoritative imams of the Hanafi school — Abu Hanifah, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani — agree on a ruling. In such a case, their collective ijtihad is considered the highest authority. No later mujtahid, even if he is qualified to exercise ijtihad, can override their agreement. The reasoning is that their understanding and evidence are superior; it is assumed that they relied on a proof inaccessible to later scholars. Thus, it is impermissible to deviate from their joint opinion. This principle establishes a strong presumption in favor of the early consensus.

Key Terms
ائمہ ثلاثہ (a'imma thalathah): The three founding imams of the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifah, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
مفتی مجتہد (mufti mujtahid): A mufti who has reached the level of independent legal reasoning (ijtihad).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling when Imam Abu Hanifah, Imam Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad all agree on a matter?
A) The mufti may choose any view he finds stronger.
B) The mufti must follow their agreement, even if he is a mujtahid.
C) The later mujtahid can exercise ijtihad to override their view.
D) The mufti follows the view of Imam Abu Hanifah alone.

Key Takeaway
The consensus of the three Hanafi founding imams is binding and cannot be overruled by later ijtihad.

Pages p. 52 · Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
